The Fortress of Fear

THE FORTRESS OF FEAR: Start-Up Options:

Press B (enter) to Begin the adventure from the First Location.

Press P (enter) to read the Prologue and Playing Instructions.
(Highly recommended if starting this adventure for the first time!)

If you have already started the adventure and wish to start from a saved position, click on the Blue Folder Icon in the taskbar above.

PLEASE NOTE: This game was envisioned as being playable Cyan On Black. Since ADRIFT does not support an authorial override of a player's colour preferences, be advised that if your background colour is not black, portions of this game will not be easily readable. For maximum experience as intended by the author please ensure your background colour is set to BLACK and the output colour to CYAN.

Before starting, please ensure that Autocomplete is unticked in the "Edit" tab in the taskbar above.

Useful Commands When Playing The Adventure:

ABOUT : BUGS : COMMANDS : CREDITS : HELP : MACROS : SPEECH : SPELLS : VOCAB

> b

By Bridge Gate
You are standing inside the Bridge Gate, which is the entrance to the Marienburg Fortress on the river side, in the southwest bailey. This part of the Fortress is known as the Lower Castle. The buildings of the Middle and High Castles loom above you to the east, beyond the low wall, moat, and curtain walls that protect them. To the north of the High Castle you see the Grand Master's Palace which is part of the Middle Castle. You can go South to the Shoemaker's Gate or North to the north end of the bailey. A portcullis under the Bridge Gate prevents your exit West from the castle.

> read plan

> x gatehouse
The part of the Bridge Gate between the towers above the entrance, it houses the mechanism that raises and lowers a portcullis which can be lowered to prevent entry and/or exit. In the wall of the gatehouse above the portcullis you see a row of downward-pointing spikes.

> drop plan
Ok, you put down the fortress plan.

> climb portcullis
You climb the portcullis using the gaps between the beams as foot and hand holds.

Top of Portcullis
You're climbing on the portcullis near the top, just underneath the gatehouse itself. Above you, a row of sharpened, downward pointing metal spikes prevent you from climbing any further. The only way you can go is back Down to the ground.

> pull spike
You grab hold of the spike with one hand and shake, push and pull it about to loosen it further. Eventually you pull it from the brickwork.

> drop spike
You drop the metal spike, which lands on the ground below.

> down
You climb back down the portcullis.

By Bridge Gate
You are standing inside the Bridge Gate, which is the entrance to the Marienburg Fortress on the river side, in the southwest bailey. This part of the Fortress is known as the Lower Castle. The buildings of the Middle and High Castles loom above you to the east, beyond the low wall, moat, and curtain walls that protect them. To the north of the High Castle you see the Grand Master's Palace which is part of the Middle Castle. You can go South to the Shoemaker's Gate or North to the north end of the bailey. A portcullis under the Bridge Gate prevents your exit West from the castle.  Also here is a metal spike and the fortress plan.

> get plan
Ok, you pick up the fortress plan.

> get spike
Ok, you pick up the metal spike.

> n
You move north.

North End of SW Bailey
You are at the north end of the southwest bailey of the fortress where the moat bends round to the east. A short distance to the East is St. Lawrence's Gate and an open archway leads North under the gatehouse into the northwest bailey.

As you approach the gate at the north end of the bailey, you feel the air around you go icy cold and you stop dead as a ghostly figure takes shape underneath the archway that leads north from here. The spectral figure is that of a short, powerfully-built man, who looks as if he was a miller in real life. He just stands there, blocking the way north.

You realise with a shock that the ghost must have been one of the lay workers who were killed when Wladyslaw's forces captured the fortress. You guess that the evil Wladyslaw has resurrected the spirit of the miller and put him here to thwart your progress. You wonder to yourself if there are any other such ghosts around the castle and how you will have to deal with them.

North End of SW Bailey
You are at the north end of the southwest bailey of the fortress where the moat bends round to the east. A short distance to the East is St. Lawrence's Gate and an open archway leads North under the gatehouse into the northwest bailey.  Standing under the archway of the gatehouse, blocking your way north, is the ghost of the miller.

> e
You move east.

By St. Lawrence's Gate
You are standing in front of St. Lawrence's Gate. An open archway leads East under the gate into the Lower Castle. The southwest bailey is to the West.

> e
You move east.

SW Corner of Lower Castle
You stand in the SW corner of the Lower Castle, an area made up of administrative and support buildings which extends over a couple of acres to the north and east. The whole area is devoid of life, giving an abandoned feel to the fortress.

A broad avenue lined with buildings leads North from here, while behind you, St. Lawrence's gate leads West to the southwest bailey of the fortress. To the North is a long building that makes up almost the whole of the west side of the Lower Castle. To the East you see a low wall that runs along the south side of the castle, the other side of which is the moat around the Middle Castle, which itself is reached by a footbridge a bit further to the east, and there are more buildings to the NE towards the centre of the Lower Castle.

Further to the east, you see another ghost standing at the entrance to the footbridge that crosses the moat - you were right! Wladyslaw has resurrected other spirits to impede your progress! You hope that getting past them is not going to be too difficult.

Looking around you realise that this fortress is vast, bigger than anything you have ever seen before. Maybe you should start by exploring the Lower Castle as fully as possible to see the areas you can get to and those that you cannot?

> n
You move north.

By St. Lawrence's Church
You stand by St. Lawrence's church at the east end, the entrance is a short distance West along a cobbled path. The church forms the south end of a long building which stretches North and makes up nearly the whole of the western side of this part of the Lower Castle. St. Lawrence's Gate is to the South, SE lies the moat in front of the Middle Castle and to the East and NE you see what appear to be farm buildings.

> ne
You move northeast.

By Farmyard
You are by the entrance to a farmyard which sits at the centre of the Lower Castle. Going East will take you into the farmyard while to the North you see a well, and you can also go West, South, NW and SW.

You catch a movement to your right and turn to face it - only to be confronted by nothing more dangerous than a grey tortoiseshell cat which comes walking out of the farmyard! The cat stops when it sees you and stares at you in that unblinking way only a cat can. You stare back for what seems like minutes before the feline tires of your attention and walks nonchalantly off in search of a rat or mouse.

> n
You move north.

By Well
You are standing by a well which lies between the smithy to the North and the farmyard to the South, you can also go NW & SW. To the east is the walled pigsty of the farmyard from which a strong smell emanates.

> lower bucket
You turn the handle of the windlass to lower the bucket down to the bottom of the well. The bucket then fills with water.

> raise bucket
You turn the handle to raise the bucket from the bottom of the well. It takes a bit more effort as the bucket is full of water.

> search bucket
You search inside the bucket and find at the bottom a key, which you take out.

> sw
You move southwest.

At South End of Long Building
You are standing at the south end of a long building which forms part of the western wall of the Lower Castle. Just here is an entrance that leads West inside the building. Carved into the top of the archway is the word "Krankenhaus". St. Lawrence's Church is to the South and going North will take you further along the building. To the East you see some farm buildings.

> s
You move south.

By Entrance to St. Lawrence's Church
You stand by the entrance to the Church of St. Lawrence, the main doors stand open and lead North inside. You can go East from here.

> n
You move north.

Inside St. Lawrence's Church
You stand inside St. Lawrence's Church, at the west end of the aisle, where the open doors lead South. The interior of the church is quite small and plain as it was used by the lay workers of the fortress for their worship. On the north wall just here hangs a large tapestry depicting scenes from the Bible. A short distance East past the pews is the pulpit, with the altar beyond that in the apse of the church.

> x tapestry
The tapestry is enormous and the biblical scenes on it must have taken many months to weave. It is hung on a rail attached to the wall of the church.  You notice a thread hanging from one edge of the tapestry.

> move tapestry
You move the tapestry a little way along its rail to reveal an archway.

Inside St. Lawrence's Church
You stand inside St. Lawrence's Church, at the west end of the aisle, where the open doors lead South. The tapestry has been moved to one side to reveal an open archway in the north wall with steps that lead Down into the crypt.

> move tapestry
You move the tapestry all the way along its rail to reveal a small niche in the wall with a lever in it.

> pull lever
You pull the lever and hear a creaking noise which seems to come from the bottom of the steps.

Foot of Steps
You're at the foot of the steps below St.Lawrence's Church. You can go back up the steps into the church and a doorway here opens North into a dark passageway that leads to the crypt.

Passageway to Crypt
You are in the passageway that leads to the crypt below St.Lawrence's Church. It is very dark down here and all you can see to the South is the foot of the steps that brought you down here. To the North is total darkness, apart from a blue light shining in the crypt.

> n
You move north.

In Crypt
You are standing in total darkness in the crypt. All you can see is the flickering flame to the north. To the south, however, you can see the passage that marks the exit from the crypt.

You move west.

In Crypt
You are standing in total darkness in the crypt. All you can see is the flickering flame on top of the altar to the southeast. A stone font stands on the floor somewhere here.

> feel font
You run your fingers over the font. They tell you that there is water in the font and there is also an inscription carved in the font just below the rim of the bowl, which is only about 30 cm wide.

> feel inscription

In Hospital
You are in the fortress hospital, which is a long, fan-vaulted hall, filled with beds, with whitewashed walls. Over by the west wall sits a desk and chair, next to which there is a small altar for the patients who are unable to attend the church next door.  The exit is East, and in the North wall a secret door has opened which leads to what looks like a storeroom.

You see a movement in the room to the north - there is somebody in there!

> look north
You look north into the storeroom. Somebody has built a barricade of crates and boxes and is hiding behind it.  Maybe you ought to find something to protect yourself with before you venture in there - whoever is in there may not be a friend!

> look into storeroom
You look north into the storeroom. Somebody has built a barricade of crates and boxes and is hiding behind it.  Maybe you ought to find something to protect yourself with before you venture in there - whoever is in there may not be a friend!

> say hello
You call out to whoever is in the storeroom, telling them you are a friend and mean no harm. There is no reply - maybe the person in there cannot understand you? They might be thinking that you mean them harm and want to defend themselves?

> e
You move east.

At South End of Long Building

By Middle of Long Building

> ne
You move northeast.

West Side of Smithy
You stand by the smithy which is situated next to the stables block. The entrance to the stables is to the North, and South is the well. To enter the smithy you need to go East. To the West, NW and SW is the long building that forms the west side of the Lower Castle.

> e
You move east.

In Smithy
You're in the Smithy, a spacious part of the building which is dominated by the forge. The walls are whitewashed to make the place as light as possible. An anvil sits in front of the forge with a metal trough just to the side of that in which the blacksmith quenches hot metal. Exits lead outside to East and West, and in the North wall there is a tall, wide doorway leading into the stables.

The hair on the back of your neck stands on end as you hear a loud growling behind you. Turning around, you expect to see a huge hound about to leap on you, but you stifle a laugh as you see that the "huge hound" is a small mongrel dog which is standing in the doorway of the smithy. You crouch down and hold out your hand, making friendly noises at the dog in an attempt to befriend it, but the dog backs away. It barks a couple of times and then runs off towards the south.

> e
You move east.

East side of Smithy
You're on the east side of the smithy, going West will take you inside. To the East is the Hexagonal Tower you can also go NE and SE to the curtain wall on either side of the tower.

> e
You move east.

By Hexagonal Tower
You stand by the Hexagonal Tower, which is part of the curtain wall on the east side of the Lower Castle. An open archway here leads East into the tower, you can go North and South along the curtain wall, and to the West you see the Smithy.

> e
You move east.

Foot of Hexagonal Tower
You are in a chamber at the foot of the Hexagonal Tower, where an open archway leads East to a spiral stairway that winds up the tower. The avenue is West through the archway.

> e
You move east.

Foot of Spiral Stairway
You are at the bottom of a spiral stairway that twists in a clockwise direction Up the Hexagonal Tower. The foot of the tower is West through the open archway here.

> u
You move up.

Spiral Stairway
You are climbing a stairway which spirals tightly Up and Down the Hexagonal Tower. An arched doorway here leads North to a chamber on the first floor of the tower. On the wall of the stairway is a torch mounted in a sconce.

> n
You move north.

1st Floor Hexagonal Tower
You're on the first floor of the Hexagonal Tower in a chamber that runs all the way round the tower.  There are a number of beds in here as well as a small altar for devotions. The room is austerely decorated with white-washed walls and an uncovered wooden floor. Four narrow, windowless embrasures, equally spaced around the walls, provide light and ventilation.  The doorway leads out South to the stairway.

> look under beds
You look under the beds and, under one of them, see something there. You reach under and your hand closes upon a soft object, which you drag out to get a better look at.

1st Floor Hexagonal Tower

The doorway leads out South to the stairway.  Also here is a scrip.

> wear scrip
You tie the scrip securely to your belt.

2nd Floor Hexagonal Tower

Four narrow, windowless embrasures, equally spaced around the walls, provide light and ventilation. One long bed must have been specially made for a giant of a man, it is over eight feet in length. The doorway leads out North to the stairway.

> look behind long bed
You look behind the long bed and find something.

In Hospital

The exit is East, and in the North wall a secret door has opened which leads to what looks like a storeroom.

> n
You move north.

In Siege Storeroom
You are in a hidden storeroom filled with stores. A barricade has been set up in front of the door here. The Hospital is South.

You see a movement behind the barricade and then you hear the click of a trigger. You instinctively raise the shield to protect yourself as a crossbow bolt whirrs towards you and hits the shield, ricocheting away.

You hear a curse then a young man stands up from where he was concealed behind the barricade. He raises both hands in the air, one of which is still holding the crossbow he used to shoot you with.

The man starts to talk to you pleadingly in Prussian, but you hold your hands out to show him you are unarmed and make him understand that you mean him no harm. He realises that you cannot speak his language and he indicates that you are to wait here, and he walks over to a cabinet on the back wall of the storeroom.

You see him unlock the cabinet and he takes something from it and returns to you. He is carrying a small vial and he mimes drinking the liquid in it and hands it to you. You do as he asks and you drink the sickly-looking green liquid, which tastes absolutely vile. You experience a momentary dizziness, which passes quickly. The man starts to talk again and to your astonishment you can understand him.

The man tells you his name is Walther and he is one of the manual workers. He relates how he was working in this storeroom when Wladyslaw's forces attacked the castle at dawn the previous day before most of the few knights that were in the fortress at the time had risen. "They appeared out of nowhere and took everyone by surprise," he tells you. "They must have known that most of the knights had left the day before to go to the aid of the people of a village who were being attacked by outlaws. I had just enough time to shut myself in here before they burst into the hospital. I thought it would only be a matter of time before they found how to get in here. I found a crossbow to defend myself but only had one bolt - as you know. I thought you were one of them."

You tell Walther what has transpired since he shut himself in here and about the task Wladyslaw has set you. He hands you the crossbow. "If you can find some bolts for this it might serve you well," he advises you. You tell Walther to stay in this room and that you will hopefully come to tell him the coast is clear when you have defeated Wladyslaw. What will happen if you fail is left unsaid. Walther bids you good luck and you leave the room. As you enter the hospital, the door slides shut behind you.

The tapestry has been moved to one side to reveal an open archway in the north wall with steps that lead Down into the crypt.  In a niche by the archway there is a lever.

You suddenly get that tingling sensation between your shoulder blades that means you are being watched. You stop and slowly look around you and up at the towers, watching out of the corners of your eyes for any movement, but you see nothing and nobody.

North side of Lower Castle

> e
 As you walk east along the side of the stables block, you catch a glimpse of a movement at the corner of the building further east, as if someone had looked around the corner at you. Running to the corner of the block, you look around the corner to see who it was, but there is no-one in sight. How strange - you could have sworn someone was there.

You notice a movement to your right and turn your head to catch a fleeting glimpse of someone running west around a corner at the south end of the Lower Castle - you were right, you had seen someone! You wonder to yourself if Prince Wladyslaw has assigned someone to spy on you?

By Main Gate

An avenue, not quite as wide as the western one, leads North from here, running alongside the eastern defensive wall of the castle where it meets a tower further north. It also goes South a short distance to the Bakery Tower, and you can go West along the moat wall to the footbridge.

You get that feeling you are being watched again, and you look around and up at the buildings and towers of the fortress. Then you spot him - a motionless figure standing at the far end of the footbridge over the moat, half-concealed by the side of the archway of the gatehouse. By Bakery
You stand by the bakery at the southern end of this side of the Lower Castle. Next to it is the Bakery Tower, so called because of its proximity to the bakery. A gatehouse forms part of the tower but a portcullis blocks the way southwards under the gate, and through it you see the southeast bailey, with the dry moat surrounding the curtain walls of the Middle and High Castles. There is an open doorway leading East into the bakery.  Here stands the ghost of the baker, who is holding a tankard in one hand.

> talk to baker
You talk to the ghost of the baker, telling him who you are.

"Bring me a tool of my trade, and you may pass within," is his only reply.

> ask baker about tool
You ask the ghost of the baker what tool he wants.

"I need a paddle so I can take the hot loaves of bread from the ovens," he tells you.

> give paddle
You hand the paddle to the baker.

He takes it from you and says, "Thank you. I can now take the bread from the ovens safely." He drains the tankard he was drinking from and hands it to you. "You may find this of use," he says, then he turns and walks into the bakery.

In Bakery
The bakery is dominated by the huge brick-built kilns in which the bread for the fortress was baked. In front of each of the four kilns is a large wooden table on which the dough was kneaded. Other cupboards and bins for the supplies used by the bakery line the walls. The door leads out West, and a wooden stairway leads Up to a storage area above the main bakery.  The ghost of the baker is here, standing in front of one of the kilns.

As you walk into the bakery, the baker turns around to face you.  "Bring me the ingredients," he tells you. "And I will bake you some bread."

> ask baker about ingredients
You ask the ghost of the baker what ingredients he needs. He sighs and shakes his head, as if he expects you to know what you need to make bread. "I will need some flour, some water and some yeast," he tells you.

> look under table

You stand by the smithy which is situated next to the stables block. The entrance to the stables is to the North, and South is the well. To enter the smithy you need to go East. To the West, NW and SW is the long building that forms the west side of the Lower Castle.

> e
You move east.

In Smithy
You're in the Smithy, a spacious part of the building which is dominated by the forge. The walls are whitewashed to make the place as light as possible. An anvil sits in front of the forge with a metal trough just to the side of that in which the blacksmith quenches hot metal. Exits lead outside to East and West, and in the North wall there is a tall, wide doorway leading into the stables.

> e
You move east.

East side of Smithy
You're on the east side of the smithy, going West will take you inside. To the East is the Hexagonal Tower you can also go NE and SE to the curtain wall on either side of the tower.

> ne
You move northeast.

North of Hexagonal Tower
You are on the east side of the Lower Castle, by the curtain wall. The Octagonal Tower is to the North and the Hexagonal Tower to the South. You can also go NW and SW, but the stables block is due west, so you cannot go in that direction.

> n
You move north.

NE Corner of Lower Castle
You stand in the NE corner of the Lower Castle, where the curtain walls on the north and east sides meet at the Octagonal Tower. An open archway here leads NE into the base of the tower and you can also go West or South from here. On the wall of the tower is a sign that reads "East Avenue".

> ne
You move northeast.

Foot of Octagonal Tower
You are in a chamber at the foot of the Octagonal Tower, where an open door leads North to a spiral stairway that winds up the tower. The Lower castle is SW through the open archway.

You are at the bottom of a spiral stairway that twists in a clockwise direction Up the Octagonal Tower. The bottom of the tower is South through the door here.

Spiral Stairway
You are climbing a stairway which spirals tightly Up and Down the Octagonal Tower. About 3/4 of the way up the wall here is an unlit torch in a metal sconce. An arched doorway leads East to a chamber on the 1st floor of the tower.

> u
You move up.

Spiral Stairway

> s
You move south.

Top Floor of Octagonal Tower
You're in a chamber at the top of the Octagonal Tower. This room is slightly better appointed than the ones lower down, maybe for knights of a higher rank. The beds look more comfortable and the altar is of much better quality. Like the lower floors, there are four embrasures equally spaced around the walls. The open archway leads North to the spiral stairway.

> put scales on altar
You place the scales on the altar. Suddenly there is a flash of bright light which dazzles you for a couple of minutes. When your vision clears, you see there is something different on the altar.

North side of Lower Castle

By Blunt Tower
You're on the north side of the Lower Castle, by the Blunt Tower. You can go West to the Buttermilk Tower, East towards the northeast corner, South to the stables and SW to the west side of the castle. There is also an open door leading North into the Blunt Tower, beside which a vine grows part of the way up the side of the tower.

> water vine
You pour the water from the tankard onto the soil around the base of the vine. The effect is almost instantaneous as the roots of the vine absorb the water. You see the leaves of the vine uncurl as water is pumped into them.

> cast vormarsch spell on vine
You cast the Vormarsch spell at the vine, being very careful to pronounce the words of the incantation properly.

The vine seems to ripple as clusters of tiny green grapes sprout from the branches and grow before your eyes into bunches of plump, juicy grapes. The spell exhausted, the sheet of parchment crumbles to dust in your hand and is blown away by the breeze.

> pick grapes
You pick a couple of bunches of grapes from the vine.

> n
You move north.

Inside Blunt Tower
You are inside the Blunt Tower, which seems to have been a storehouse for the fortress brewery, judging by the large barrels that fill the room. The door out is to the South, and wooden stairs wind Up the wall to the floor above.

> drop all
Ok, you put down the Bible, the piece of paper, the brass key, the iron key, the metal spike, the altar cloth, the tankard, the large shield, the broken silver key, the bunches of grapes, the besom, the crossbow, the glass vial and the fortress plan.

> roll barrel
You roll one of the barrels to one side to reveal the shrine by the wall.

Inside Blunt Tower

> put tankard on shrine
You place the tankard on the shrine.

> pray to bacchus
You bow your head and say a brief prayer to Bacchus, asking that he turn the grape juice into wine. You expect nothing to happen, but then you hear a childish giggle and look up to see a tiny winged cherub hovering above the shrine. The cherub swoops down and touches the tankard with one of its tiny chubby hands. It then flies up and hovers in front of your astonished face, giggling mischievously. "Good health, Duke Alaric!" it says in a tiny voice. "Thank you for watering my vine," then it vanishes with a pop of misplaced air.

> get tankard
(from the shrine)
Ok, you take the tankard from the shrine.

On the north wall just here hangs a large tapestry depicting scenes from the Bible. A short distance East past the pews is the pulpit, with the altar beyond that in the apse of the church.  The tapestry has been moved to one side to reveal an open archway in the north wall with steps that lead Down into the crypt.  In a niche by the archway there is a lever.

You are climbing a stairway which spirals tightly Up and Down the Hexagonal Tower. An arched doorway here leads North to a chamber on the first floor of the tower. On the wall of the stairway is a torch mounted in a sconce.

> u
You move up.

Spiral Stairway
You are climbing a stairway which spirals tightly Up and Down the Hexagonal Tower. About 3/4 of the way up the wall just here is a metal sconce which has an unlit reed torch in it. An arched doorway here leads South to a chamber on the second floor of the tower.

> u
You move up.

Top of Spiral Stairway
You are at the top of the spiral stairway in the Hexagonal Tower, you can only go Down from here. To the North there is a door.

> unlock door with gold key
You unlock the door with the gold key.

> push door
You push the door open.

> n
You move north.

Top Floor of Hexagonal Tower
You're in a chamber at the top of the Hexagonal Tower. This is used as an office judging by the desk and other furniture. The door leads out South to the spiral stairway.   Sitting behind the desk you see the ghost of the procurator.

As you walk into the room, you see a ghost sitting behind the desk. He looks up in surprise as you enter, then his expression changes to one of expectation.

"Hello young man, have you brought me hope?" the ghost asks you.

> talk to procurator
You tell the ghost of the procurator who you are and what your quest here is, but he seems totally disinterested in what you tell him. He just looks at you with mournful eyes and says, "Is there any hope for me at all, Duke Alaric?"

> s
You move south.

Top of Spiral Stairway
You are at the top of the spiral stairway in the Hexagonal Tower, you can only go Down from here. To the North there is a door.

> d

You move south.

Halfway along East Avenue
You are about halfway along the eastern avenue of the Lower Castle, just south of the Hexagonal Tower, which you can get to by going North. To the east of you is a building, in which there are large double doors, which is joined to the base of the tower to the South of you. In the stone lintel above the doors are carved the words Armourer's Workshop.

> s
You move south.

By Armourer's Tower
You stand by a tower on the east side of the Lower Castle. The entrance to the tower is via a wooden door under an archway which leads East. The tower is joined to a two-storey building which extends north towards the Hexagonal Tower. To the West you see a farmyard with a couple of buildings to the north & south of it.  Hanging from a brass knocker on the door of the tower is a small sign.

> w
You move west.

East end of Farmyard
You are at the east end of the farmyard, where you see a chicken house to the North and a shed to the South. The farmyard extends West and going East will take you to the east side of the Lower Castle.  Here you see the ghost of the Farmer's Wife.

> say hello to wife
You try to talk to the ghost of the farmer's wife, but she just wrings her hands. "The Komtur will be doing his daily inspection soon," she says in a worried voice, "and I have lost my besom."

> ask wife about tool
The ghost of the wife doesn't appear to understand you.

> w
You move west.

West end of Farmyard
You're at the west end of the farmyard, where to the north there is a pigsty and to the South a byre, both surrounded by low walls. The farmyard continues East and you can also go West out into the Lower Castle.

> w
You move west.

By Farmyard
You are by the entrance to a farmyard which sits at the centre of the Lower Castle. Going East will take you into the farmyard while to the North you see a well, and you can also go West, South, NW and SW.

> sw
You move southwest.

By St. Lawrence's Church
You stand by St. Lawrence's church at the east end, the entrance is a short distance West along a cobbled path. The church forms the south end of a long building which stretches North and makes up nearly the whole of the western side of this part of the Lower Castle. St. Lawrence's Gate is to the South, SE lies the moat in front of the Middle Castle and to the East and NE you see what appear to be farm buildings.

> w
You move west.

By Entrance to St. Lawrence's Church
You stand by the entrance to the Church of St. Lawrence, the main doors stand open and lead North inside. You can go East from here.

> n
You move north.

Inside St. Lawrence's Church
You stand inside St. Lawrence's Church, at the west end of the aisle, where the open doors lead South. The interior of the church is quite small and plain as it was used by the lay workers of the fortress for their worship. On the north wall just here hangs a large tapestry depicting scenes from the Bible. A short distance East past the pews is the pulpit, with the altar beyond that in the apse of the church.  The tapestry has been moved to one side to reveal an open archway in the north wall with steps that lead Down into the crypt.  In a niche by the archway there is a lever.

> d
You move down.

Foot of Steps
You're at the foot of the steps below St.Lawrence's Church. You can go back up the steps into the church and a doorway here opens North into a dark passageway that leads to the crypt.

> n
You move north.

Passageway to Crypt
You are in the passageway that leads to the crypt below St.Lawrence's Church. It is very dark down here and all you can see to the South is the foot of the steps that brought you down here. To the North is total darkness, apart from a blue light shining in the crypt.

> n
You move north.

In Crypt
You are standing in total darkness in the crypt. All you can see is the flickering flame to the north. To the south, however, you can see the passage that marks the exit from the crypt.

> e
You move east.

In Crypt
You are standing in almost total darkness in the crypt. All you can see is the flame flickering on the altar to the northwest.  A small altar stands in the corner here, although it is invisible in the darkness.

> pray to charity
You kneel and whisper a short prayer to the God of Charity. As you get to your feet you sense that something is now standing on the altar.

> feel altar
You run your hands over the altar and you feel an object that is now standing on the altar. Your questing fingers reveal it is a goblet, which you take. You will have to get it into the light to examine it better.

> nw
You move northwest.

In Crypt
You are standing in the darkened crypt, by an altar on which burns an eternal flame. The light cast by this is not enough to illuminate the rest of the crypt, which is in total darkness. To the south, however, you can just make out the exit from the crypt.

> nw
You move northwest.

In Crypt

> fill goblet with water

> give goblet to procurator
You offer the goblet to the ghost of the Procurator. He takes it and drinks the water.

As he drains the goblet, a look of pure joy appears on his face. "There is hope for me after all!" he exclaims. As his ghostly form starts to fade away, he reaches into a pocket and takes something out of it which he places on the desk in front of him.

Just before he disappears from view, he raises a hand in farewell and you hear a ghostly voice whisper, "Good luck with your mission, Duke Alaric!".

By Stables

Wide double doors lead East into the stables, while to the South, at the other end of the building, is the Smithy. In the upper part of the stables you see the opening of a hayloft with a derrick fixed to the wall beside it.  A rope hangs down from the derrick to the ground.  Here, standing in the doorway to the stables, is the ghost of the farrier.

> give hoofpick to farrier
You hand the hoofpick to the ghost of the farrier.

"Thank you, Duke Alaric," he says, with a huge grin. "Now I can tend to my horses." He turns around and walks into the stables, fading from view as he does so.

In Stables
You're in the stables, where you see many stalls for the knight's horses. Although there are no horses here now, the lingering smell of horse sweat and manure, saddle soap, hay, and hoof oil mingle in an odour which is almost overpowering. An open doorway leads East between two of the stalls into the tack room, the way out is West through double doors, and there is another wide open doorway at the South end leading into the Smithy.  A ladder here leads up to a trapdoor in the ceiling.  Also here is a sack hook.

> get sack hook

You are in the tack room at the back of the stables, where saddles, bridles and other equine equipment and accoutrements are stored all over the place, including hanging from the rafters. The smell of leather and polish is almost overpowering, but it has a fragrance you are very familiar with and like a lot.

> look up

North End of SW Bailey
You are at the north end of the southwest bailey of the fortress where the moat bends round to the east. A short distance to the East is St. Lawrence's Gate and an open archway leads North under the gatehouse into the northwest bailey.  Standing under the archway of the gatehouse, blocking your way north, is the ghost of the miller.

> ask miller about tool
You talk to the ghost of the miller. "Bring me a tool of my trade, and you may pass within," is his only reply.

> give sack hook to miller
You hand the sack hook to the ghost of the miller. He takes it from you and says,"Thank you," with a nod. The ghost walks away from you and turns north, leaving the way under the tower clear.

North End of SW Bailey

South End of NW Bailey
You are in the northwest bailey by the south end of the castle granaries, which stand on the west side of the bailey. These are long warehouses in which the grain produced by the farms surrounding the fortress was stored. You can go North, South over the moat & under the tower to the southwest bailey, and West into the granary.

> n
You move north.

North End of NW Bailey
You are at the north end of the northwest bailey, standing in front of the castle mill with the northern entrance to the granaries to your left. To the north, rising above the mill, you can see the Tetragonal Tower, so-called as it has 10 sides. You can only go South along the granary building, West into the granaries, or North into the mill.  Standing here, blocking your way into the mill, is the ghost of the miller.

You hear a loud cawing noise which startles you slightly, and you look up to see a couple of large black crows looking down at you from a rooftop on the east side of the bailey. You shiver as you wonder if they would peck out your eyeballs if you were a corpse lying on the ground. Picking up a pebble lying on the ground, you throw it at the crows, which squawk in alarm. They launch themselves off the rooftop and flap away over the granaries toward the river.

> x miller
The miller was a short, squat man with muscular arms and chest. You notice now that he has a small tattoo on his right arm.

> ask miller about tattoo
You talk to the ghost of the miller. "Bring me a tool of my trade, and you may pass within," is his only reply.

> ask miller about tool
You talk to the ghost of the miller. "Bring me a tool of my trade, and you may pass within," is his only reply.

> w
You move west.

North End of Granaries
You are at the north end of the castle granaries. This is much the same as the south end, with another brick silo for storing grain which you can go Up into. You can go South, or East outside into the outer bailey. There is also a pair of huge doors beyond the silo which are closed.

> s
You move south.

South End of Granaries
You are in the castle granaries, at the south end. This is a cavernous building, large enough to allow whole wagons to be driven in to be loaded and unloaded. On the west side of the building you see a brick-built silo which you can go Up into, there is another at the other end of the granary to the North, while going East leads to the outer bailey.  Also here is a farm wagon.

> push wagon north
You set your shoulder against the wagon and push. It takes some strength, but the wagon rolls to the north end of the granaries.

North End of Granaries
You are at the north end of the castle granaries. This is much the same as the south end, with another brick silo for storing grain which you can go Up into. You can go South, or East outside into the outer bailey. There is also a pair of huge doors beyond the silo which are closed.  Also here is a farm wagon.

> climb wagon
You climb up onto the wagon.

On Wagon
You are standing on the wagon in front of the seat. You are quite high up and the rafters of the granary roof are just above your head. You can Climb Down to the floor of the granary from here, or you could even Jump Down if you were feeling energetic!

> look up
You see the rafters of the granary roof less than a metre above your head.

> d
You climb down off the wagon to the floor of the granary.

North End of Granaries
You are at the north end of the castle granaries. This is much the same as the south end, with another brick silo for storing grain which you can go Up into. You can go South, or East outside into the outer bailey. There is also a pair of huge doors beyond the silo which are closed.  Also here is a farm wagon.

> u
You move up.

In Silo (North)
You are in one of the grain silos. It is about 4 meters wide and the same deep and the 3 meter high walls reach almost to the rafters under the roof of the granary. Steps go Down to the floor of the north end of the granaries.

> search silo
While the silo is empty of sacks you notice a scattering of grains of wheat on the floor of the silo.

In Silo (North)
You are in one of the grain silos. It is about 4 meters wide and the same deep and the 3 meter high walls reach almost to the rafters under the roof of the granary. Steps go Down to the floor of the north end of the granaries.  The floor of the silo is scattered with grains of wheat.

> sweep grains with besom
You sweep the grains of wheat scattered on the floor of the silo into a small pile with the besom. It only takes you a minute or so.

In Silo (North)
You are in one of the grain silos. It is about 4 meters wide and the same deep and the 3 meter high walls reach almost to the rafters under the roof of the granary. Steps go Down to the floor of the north end of the granaries.  Also here is a pile of wheat.

> e
You move east.

North End of NW Bailey
You are at the north end of the northwest bailey, standing in front of the castle mill with the northern entrance to the granaries to your left. To the north, rising above the mill, you can see the Tetragonal Tower, so-called as it has 10 sides. You can only go South along the granary building, West into the granaries, or North into the mill.  Standing here, blocking your way into the mill, is the ghost of the miller.

> s
You move south.

South End of NW Bailey
You are in the northwest bailey by the south end of the castle granaries, which stand on the west side of the bailey. These are long warehouses in which the grain produced by the farms surrounding the fortress was stored. You can go North, South over the moat & under the tower to the southwest bailey, and West into the granary.

> s
You move south.

North End of SW Bailey
You are at the north end of the southwest bailey of the fortress where the moat bends round to the east. A short distance to the East is St. Lawrence's Gate and an open archway leads North under the gatehouse into the northwest bailey.

> e
You move east.

By St. Lawrence's Gate
You are standing in front of St. Lawrence's Gate. An open archway leads East under the gate into the Lower Castle. The southwest bailey is to the West.

> e
You move east.

SW Corner of Lower Castle
You are in the SW corner of the Lower Castle. You can go East, West, North and NE from here.

> n
You move north.

By St. Lawrence's Church
You stand by St. Lawrence's church at the east end, the entrance is a short distance West along a cobbled path. The church forms the south end of a long building which stretches North and makes up nearly the whole of the western side of this part of the Lower Castle. St. Lawrence's Gate is to the South, SE lies the moat in front of the Middle Castle and to the East and NE you see what appear to be farm buildings.

> ne
You move northeast.

By Farmyard
You are by the entrance to a farmyard which sits at the centre of the Lower Castle. Going East will take you into the farmyard while to the North you see a well, and you can also go West, South, NW and SW.

> e
You move east.

West end of Farmyard
You're at the west end of the farmyard, where to the north there is a pigsty and to the South a byre, both surrounded by low walls. The farmyard continues East and you can also go West out into the Lower Castle.

> s
You move south.

In Byre
You are in the byre, south of the farmyard. A cow is tethered here and stands munching hay from a rack attached to the wall that surrounds the byre. The farmyard is North.

> search hay
You rummage through the hay in the hayrack - OUCH! Something sharp pierces your thumb. You pull your hand out of the hay and find a needle sticking in it. You pull the needle out and suck your thumb to stop it bleeding.

> n
You move north.

West end of Farmyard
You're at the west end of the farmyard, where to the north there is a pigsty and to the South a byre, both surrounded by low walls. The farmyard continues East and you can also go West out into the Lower Castle.

> n
You move north.

In Pigsty
You are in a pigsty, which is surrounded by a wall and the only exit is South to the farmyard.  Lying against the wall of the pigsty is a huge sow, surrounded by her piglets.

> prick sow with needle
You jab the sow in her meaty hindquarters with the needle. She gives vent to a roar of indignation and lurches to her feet, scattering her piglets in all directions. You quickly run out of the pigsty with the angry sow in pursuit, her teeth snapping at your heels. Fortunately she is too lazy to sustain the chase, so she gives up her attack on you and returns to the pigsty to resume her sleep which you so rudely interrupted.

West end of Farmyard
You're at the west end of the farmyard, where to the north there is a pigsty and to the South a byre, both surrounded by low walls. The farmyard continues East and you can also go West out into the Lower Castle.

> get rod
Ok, you pick up the green rod.

You move south.

East end of Farmyard
You are at the east end of the farmyard, where you see a chicken house to the North and a shed to the South. The farmyard extends West and going East will take you to the east side of the Lower Castle.  Here you see the ghost of the Farmer's Wife.

> give besom to wife
You hand the besom to the ghost of the farmer's wife.  "Now I can sweep the farmyard," she says happily. She walks to the other end of the farmyard and starts to sweep it, singing softly to herself.

East end of Farmyard
You are at the east end of the farmyard, where you see a chicken house to the North and a shed to the South. The farmyard extends West and going East will take you to the east side of the Lower Castle.

In Shed
You are in the shed, which is crammed with farming equipment and tools. Double doors lead out North to the farmyard.  Also here is a stool.

> get stool
Ok, you pick up the stool.

> search tools
You search through the tools and find a trowel that might be useful to you. You wonder, however if you search again you might find something else more useful?

West end of Farmyard

In Byre

> drop stool
Ok, you put down the stool.

> milk cow
You sit down on the stool and place the pail under the cow's udders. You start to pull and squeeze her teats and, to your amazement, milk starts to spurt out of the teats almost immediately. Once or twice the cow looks round at you and moos, as if to say "Go easy!", but eventually you have a full pail of milk and the cow is looking a lot happier.

> get pail
Ok, you pick up the metal pail.

> saw stool
You saw one of the legs off the stool with the saw.

> get leg
You are already carrying the wooden leg!

By St. Lawrence's Church

By Entrance to St. Lawrence's Church
You stand by the entrance to the Church of St. Lawrence, the main doors stand open and lead North inside. You can go East from here.

> n
You move north.

Inside St. Lawrence's Church
You stand inside St. Lawrence's Church, at the west end of the aisle, where the open doors lead South. The interior of the church is quite small and plain as it was used by the lay workers of the fortress for their worship. On the north wall just here hangs a large tapestry depicting scenes from the Bible. A short distance East past the pews is the pulpit, with the altar beyond that in the apse of the church.  The tapestry has been moved to one side to reveal an open archway in the north wall with steps that lead Down into the crypt.  In a niche by the archway there is a lever.

> pull thread
You pull the thread away from the tapestry, it is much longer than the bit that was sticking out!

> thread needle
You firstly put the end of the thread into your mouth to damp it so that the fibres stick together. Pursing your lips in concentration, you carefully push the end of the thread through the eye of the needle. This is quite easy as the eye of the needle is quite a large one, and you pull the thread through and knot the ends together.

> s
You move south.

At South End of Long Building
You are standing at the south end of a long building which forms part of the western wall of the Lower Castle. Just here is an entrance that leads West inside the building. Carved into the archway is the word "Hospital". St. Lawrence's Church is to the South and going North will take you further along the building. To the East you see some farm buildings.

> n
You move north.

By Middle of Long Building
You are roughly at the middle of the long building which runs along the west side of the Lower Castle. You can go North and South along the building, while to the East you see a well. You can also go SE and NE.

> n
You move north.

Near North End of Long Building
You are near the north end of the long building where an open door leads West inside. Carved into the top of the archway are the words "Manual Worker's Residence". Going North will take you to the north end corner of the building, South to the middle of the building, and to the East you see the castle smithy.

> ne
You move northeast.

By Stables
You are standing by the stables, which is a long, tall building standing separately from the others. Wide double doors lead East into the stables, while to the South, at the other end of the building, is the Smithy. In the upper part of the stables you see the opening of a hayloft with a derrick fixed to the wall beside it.  A rope hangs down from the derrick to the ground.

> e
You move east.

In Stables
You're in the stables, where you see many stalls for the knight's horses. Although there are no horses here now, the lingering smell of horse sweat and manure, saddle soap, hay, and hoof oil mingle in an odour which is almost overpowering. An open doorway leads East between two of the stalls into the tack room, the way out is West through double doors, and there is another wide open doorway at the South end leading into the Smithy.  A ladder here leads up to a trapdoor in the ceiling.

> search stalls
You search in some of the stalls but you find nothing apart from a piece of old sacking.

In Stables
You're in the stables, where you see many stalls for the knight's horses. Although there are no horses here now, the lingering smell of horse sweat and manure, saddle soap, hay, and hoof oil mingle in an odour which is almost overpowering. An open doorway leads East between two of the stalls into the tack room, the way out is West through double doors, and there is another wide open doorway at the South end leading into the Smithy.  A ladder here leads up to a trapdoor in the ceiling.  Also here is some hessian sacking material.

> get material
Ok, you pick up the hessian sacking material.

> sew material
You fold the sacking in half and sew up two of the open sides with a simple running stitch to form a small sack. When you have tied off the second row of stitching, you turn the sack inside out to hide the stitching, just like you remember your mother doing.

> w
You move west.

Hallway of Residence
You are in the main hallway of the residence of the manual workers. To the North and South doorways lead into dormitories, while the refectory for the workers is through a doorway at the West end of the hallway. An open door leads East to the avenue outside.

> s
You move south.

South Dormitory
You are in the south dormitory, which is a long room with white-washed walls and a tiled floor. There are rows of beds along both walls, and at one end a small altar. Each bed has a chest at the foot of it. The hallway is to the North.

> put bible on altar
You place the Bible on the altar. Suddenly there is a flash of bright light which dazzles you for a couple of minutes. When your vision clears, you see there is something different on the altar.

South Dormitory

> get vellum

> w

Refectory
You are in the refectory, which is a large room filled with rows of long tables which have benches either side, where the manual workers of the fortress would take their meals. The hallway is East and a door leads West into the kitchen.

> w
You move west.

Kitchen
This is the kitchen where the meals for the manual workers are prepared, a large room with all manner of nooks and crannies. There are two large tables for food preparation, a chopping block and two ovens in which food was cooked. In the north wall there is a huge fireplace in which there is a spit on which animals could be roasted. The walls are festooned with cooking implements and tools, and a drying rack hangs from the ceiling. The only exit is East into the refectory.

> enter fireplace
You enter the fireplace, ducking your head to avoid hitting it on the lintel.....

In Fireplace
You are standing in the fireplace, where there is a large spit as well as other metal contraptions for hanging pots and kettles on. The ashes of the last fire lay in the shallow firepit here and above you is the chimney shaft. The kitchen is to the South.

> fill vial with soot
You scrape some soot from the chimney shaft into the glass vial and replace the stopper firmly.

> search ashes
You search through the ashes in the firepit and your fingers close upon a metal object. You pick it up and see that it is just a small knife.

> s
You move south.

In Shed
You are in the shed, which is crammed with farming equipment and tools. Double doors lead out North to the farmyard.  Here you see a quernstone.

> put leg in hole
You insert the leg of the stool into the small hole in the side of the quernstone - it is a perfect fit and you now have a handle with which to turn the quernstone.

> pour wheat into quern
You pour the grains of wheat from the sack into the hole in the top of the quernstone.

> turn handle
You turn the handle of the quernstone and the grains of wheat are ground into flour, which falls into the box under the quernstone.

> get flour
You fill the hessian sack with flour from the box.

You stand by a tower on the east side of the Lower Castle. The entrance to the tower is via a wooden door under an archway which leads East. The tower is joined to a two-storey building which extends north towards the Hexagonal Tower. To the West you see a farmyard with a couple of buildings to the north & south of it.  Hanging from a brass knocker on the door of the tower is a small sign.

You move north.

In the stone lintel above the doors are carved the words Armourer's Workshop.

> n
You move north.

North of Hexagonal Tower

> nw
You move northwest.

North side of Lower Castle
You are by the north wall of the Lower Castle, just by the corner of the stables block. You can go West towards the Blunt Tower, East to the NE corner of the Lower Castle and SE. The stables block to the south prevents you going in that direction and southwest as well.

> w
You move west.

North side of Lower Castle
You are by the north wall of the Lower Castle, just east of the Blunt Tower. You can only go East and West from here, the stables block is to the south, preventing you from going south, southwest & southeast.  Also here is a long plank.

> w
You move west.

By Blunt Tower
You're on the north side of the Lower Castle, by the Blunt Tower. You can go West to the Buttermilk Tower, East towards the northeast corner, South to the stables and SW to the west side of the castle. There is also an open door leading North into the Blunt Tower, beside which a vine grows part of the way up the side of the tower.

> n
You move north.

Inside Blunt Tower
You are inside the Blunt Tower, which seems to have been a storehouse for the fortress brewery, judging by the large barrels that fill the room. The door out is to the South, and wooden stairs wind Up the wall to the floor above.  Against the wall behind the barrels is a small shrine.

> u
You move up.

1st floor of Blunt Tower
You are on the first floor of the Blunt Tower, which is the only upper floor of this short tower. The room is a jumble of old equipment, much of which looks as if it was used for brewing.  Stairs lead Down to the bottom of the Tower and on the West side of the room the wooden shelves have been moved aside to reveal an open archway leading West to a bridge that you can cross to the Buttermilk Tower.  Also here is a winepress.

> w
You move west.

Bridge between Towers
You're on the enclosed bridge linking the Buttermilk Tower to the Blunt Tower. Embrasures on either side of the bridge provide light to see by.  You can go East past the shelves that you moved to one side into the tower.

> w
You move west.

1st Floor Buttermilk Tower
You're on the first floor of the Buttermilk Tower. The stairs going  up to the top floor of the tower have collapsed, so you can only go back Down. However, on the East side of the tower there is an open archway that leads to an enclosed bridge that connects this tower to the top floor of the Blunt tower next door.

> d
You move down.

Bottom of Buttermilk Tower
You are at the bottom of the Buttermilk Tower. The door leads out South and a flight of wooden stairs winding around the wall goes Up to the first floor. This part of the tower was once used as a dairy, but now it seems to be used as storeroom for unwanted and broken equipment.  Also here is a butter churn.

> pour milk into churn
You pour the milk from the pail into the butter churn.

> turn churn
You turn the handle of the butter churn so that the barrel is rotating.  You hear the milk sloshing around inside.

> cast wachstum spell at churn
You cast the WACHSTUM spell at the butter churn, and it immediately starts to turn faster and faster.....

You hear the milk sloshing around inside, but then it starts to congeal and after a minute or two you hear it thudding as it has turned into a lump of butter.....

The barrel slows down and then stops. The spell exhausted, the sheet of vellum crumbles into dust, which trickles through your fingers onto the floor.

> u
You move up.

1st Floor Buttermilk Tower
You're on the first floor of the Buttermilk Tower. The stairs going  up to the top floor of the tower have collapsed, so you can only go back Down. By Main Gate

> s
You move south.

By Bakery
You stand by the bakery at the southern end of this side of the Lower Castle. Next to it is the Bakery Tower, so called because of its proximity to the bakery. A gatehouse forms part of the tower but a portcullis blocks the way southwards under the gate, and through it you see the southeast bailey, with the dry moat surrounding the curtain walls of the Middle and High Castles. There is an open doorway leading East into the bakery.

> e
You move east.

In Bakery
The bakery is dominated by the huge brick-built kilns in which the bread for the fortress was baked. In front of each of the four kilns is a large wooden table on which the dough was kneaded. Other cupboards and bins for the supplies used by the bakery line the walls. The door leads out West, and a wooden stairway leads Up to a storage area above the main bakery.  The ghost of the baker is here, standing in front of one of the kilns.

> ask baker about bread
"It is what I spend half my day baking," the ghost of the baker tells you in a toneless voice.

> give flour to baker
You hand the sack of flour to the ghost of the baker.

"Thank you," he intones, "that is sufficient for my needs."

> give pail to baker
You hand the pail of water to the ghost of the baker.

"Thank you," he intones, "that is sufficient for my needs."

Now he has all three ingredients, the baker sets to work. You watch, mouth agape, as the ghost whizzes around the bakery, mixing the ingredients, kneading the dough, putting the dough into a tin and then putting that into one of the ovens. After only a few minutes, he takes the tin out of the oven using the paddle you gave to him earlier and you smell the wonderful aroma of freshly baked bread.

He tips the baked loaf of bread out of the tin, cuts a thick slice from it and hands it to you. "I thank you, Duke Alaric," the ghost tells you. "I will have the rest of the bread for my lunch." As his ghostly form starts to fade he extends his arm towards you and you see that he is holding the silver key - now whole - in his hand. "I have repaired your key, you will be able to open the other door now," he tells you as you take it from him.

As you mutter an astonished "Thank you," the ghost nods his head and fades from view.

In Bakery
The bakery is dominated by the huge brick-built kilns in which the bread for the fortress was baked. In front of each of the four kilns is a large wooden table on which the dough was kneaded. Other cupboards and bins for the supplies used by the bakery line the walls. The door leads out West, and a wooden stairway leads Up to a storage area above the main bakery.  Also here is a small hessian sack.

You see a movement out of the corner of your eye and see the ghost of the farrier walking towards you. He stops when he reaches you and picks up the pail.

"I beg your pardon, Duke Alaric," he says apologetically. "I need the pail to fetch water for my horses."

He walks away taking the pail with him, fading from view as he goes, but just as his form disappears for ever you hear his voice whisper, "You won't be needing it again anyway."

An open doorway leads East between two of the stalls into the tack room, the way out is West through double doors, and there is another wide open doorway at the South end leading into the Smithy.  A ladder here leads up to a trapdoor in the ceiling.

By Footbridge to Middle Castle
You are by the footbridge that crosses a wide moat to the Middle Castle. You can go South across the footbridge, East and West alongside the moat and also NW.  Here stands the ghost of the sentry.

> talk to sentry
You talk to the ghost of the sentry. He stares impassively ahead and says, in a deep, gravelly voice, "I am hungry, Duke Alaric, bring me some food and you may pass."

> ask sentry about food
You ask the ghost of the sentry what food he would prefer.

"I am a simple man with simple tastes, Duke Alaric," the knight tells you. "Maybe some bread and butter?"

> give bread to sentry
You hand the slice of bread to the ghost of the sentry.

He takes it and eats it, relishing every mouthful. As the last crumb is finished, he smiles and says, "I thank you, Duke Alaric, my hunger is now sated."

He reaches inside his overtunic and takes out a coin. He flips it into the air towards you and you catch it. "A little something for your trouble," he tells you. "I must now take up my duty at the Main Gate."

He raises his massive sword into the air to salute you and he walks off to the east - the footbridge to the Middle Castle is now clear to cross.

Gap between buildings
You are on a path in a gap between the buildings of the Middle Castle and the curtain wall that protects them. Ahead of you to the South the path leads into an open archway that passes through the castle buildings, which loom high above you. Above the archway hangs a heavy wooden portcullis. To East and West are paths leading between the curtain wall and the buildings, while going North will take you to the footbridge across the inner moat.

> s
You move south.

North Side of Courtyard
You are on the north side of the Middle Castle Courtyard, by the open archway under the building that leads North to the footbridge over the outer moat. The courtyard is bounded by the Grand Master's Palace on the west side and the Knight's Hall on the east and there is just a low wall on the south side where you see the High Castle looming above the curtain walls that surround it. You can go South, East, West, SE and SW across the courtyard.

You stand and survey the courtyard of the Middle Castle that you have at last reached. Your attention is immediately drawn to a ghostly figure kneeling by a small flower bed in the centre of the courtyard, while over on the east side of the courtyard you see what appear to be two large statues standing in front of some exits. Looking left, you see an even larger statue of a mounted knight a short distance further east.

You once again get a crawling sensation running up and down your back which means you are being observed by someone of flesh and blood. Sure enough, in the far distance at the opposite end of the courtyard you see the figure of a man standing on the footbridge which crosses the inner moat to the High Castle. You get the impression from his stance that he is waiting for you to approach the footbridge. Dare you take that risk.....

> look

Here, blocking the archway to the north, is a huge statue of a mounted Teutonic Knight.

East Side (South)

You move south.

SE Corner by Chapel
You are in the SE corner of the Middle Castle, where St. Therese's Chapel stands at the south end of the Knight's Hall. The courtyard extends North, West and NW from here and double doors under an archway lead East into the chapel. The south side of the castle is open, with just a narrow grass bank in front of a low wall that overlooks the inner moat. On the far side of the moat are the massive curtain walls of the High Castle, the buildings of which soar into the sunny sky.

As you approach the wall on the south side of the courtyard you look to your right and see the man, whom you saw earlier, standing on the middle of the footbridge over the moat. You notice he is dressed in a robe and he just stands there looking at you, his arms akimbo. You guess that he is Prince Wladyslaw himself.

"Let's see how you get past this!" he calls out to you in a heavily-accented voice and, raising his arms to point at the gatehouse, he mouths the words of an incantation. You instinctively flinch as the archway under the gatehouse is filled with a corruscation of purple and red sparks, accompanied by a loud sizzling noise and a lot of white smoke!

When the pyrotechnic display clears, you see that a solid wall now fills the archway. When you look over at the footbridge again, Wladyslaw is no longer in sight.

> w
You move west.

South Side by Gatehouse
You are standing by the gatehouse that guards the bridge over the inner moat that leads South to the High Castle. You can go East and West alongside the wall that overlooks the inner moat, North towards the northern exit, and NW and NE. On the ground just here are the two massive wooden doors that once stood under the gatehouse, the archway under it is filled with a solid wall of granite blocks.

> w
You move west.

SW Corner of MC
You are in the southwest of the Middle Castle, by the southern entrance to the cloister that runs the whole length of the Grand Master's Palace that makes up the west side of the castle. An open archway leads West into the cloister and you can also go North, NE and East. The south side of the castle is open, with just a narrow grass bank in front of a low wall that overlooks the inner moat. On the far side of the moat are the massive curtain walls of the High Castle, the buildings of which soar into the sky.

Cloisters South (Middle)

> read note
The message on the note reads:

"Come to the refectory, Duke Alaric, I will be waiting for you there." It is signed "The Cellarer".

As you look at the note wondering who the cellarer is, the note crumbles to dust in your hands.

Middle of MC Courtyard
You stand in the centre of the courtyard, where there is a small circular flowerbed in which sits a solitary rosebush. You can go in all directions from here. The ghost of the gardener is here, kneeling by the flower bed, looking at the sole remaining rose on the dead rosebush.

As you approach the ghost, it stands up and turns to face you.

"Look what they have done to my pride and joy," the ghost says mournfully to you, gesturing towards the rosebush. "It has died and I was unable to save it."

His head hung in sorrow, the ghost of the gardener walks slowly away, gradually fading from view.

Hallway of Residence

> w
You move west.

Refectory
You are in the refectory, which is a large room filled with rows of long tables which have benches either side, where the manual workers of the fortress would take their meals. The hallway is East and a door leads West into the kitchen.  Sitting at one of the tables is the ghost of the cellarer.

As you walk into the refectory you are aware of the faint smell of almonds in the air and the rustle of paper. Then you notice the ghostly figure of an old man sitting at one of the tables, eating something from a paper bag he holds in his hand. As you approach the ghost of the Cellarer - for it can be only he - the figure gets to his feet and inclines his head in greeting.

"I see you found my note, Duke Alaric," he says in a quavering voice. "Thank you for coming. I have been instructed to give you a cryptic clue to help with your mission, and it is this: 'Advisorily speaking, it is a colourful and uplifting way to gain entry to those places you cannot yet reach.'"

As you try to work out the meaning of his speech, his spectral form starts to fade away. Before you have a chance to speak, he raises his hand in farewell, saying, "Pray for me, Duke Alaric, good luck!" As he disappears from view you catch the scent of almonds and a rustle of paper once again.

To East and West are paths leading between the curtain wall and the buildings, while going North will take you to the footbridge across the inner moat.

> s
You move south.

North Side of Courtyard
You are on the north side of the Middle Castle Courtyard, by the open archway under the building that leads North to the footbridge over the outer moat. The courtyard is bounded by the Grand Master's Palace on the west side and the Knight's Hall on the east and there is just a low wall on the south side where you see the High Castle looming above the curtain walls that surround it. You can go South, East, West, SE and SW across the courtyard.

> e
You move east.

North side of Courtyard(E)
You are on the north side of the Middle Castle Courtyard, where an open archway leads North to steps going down into darkness. Carved into the lintel of the archway are the words "Furnace Vaults". You can also go East, West and SE from here. It is sunny here but the buildings on the east side cast a shadow on the ground.  Here, blocking the archway to the north, is a huge statue of a mounted Teutonic Knight.

> prop ladder against statue
You prop the ladder against the statue of the mounted knight.

By Walled Byre
You stand by a wall which surrounds a byre in which a single cow stands forlornly munching hay from a rack attached to the other side of the wall. The wall is just low enough for you to see over, and you will be able to get into the byre from the farmyard further North. You can also go NW, West, SW, South and SE from here. Fixed to the wall is a sign which reads "West Avenue".

West Side of Smithy
You stand by the smithy which is situated next to the stables block. The entrance to the stables is to the North, and South is the well. To enter the smithy you need to go East. To the West, NW and SW is the long building that forms the west side of the Lower Castle.

> n
You move north.

By Stables
You are standing by the stables, which is a long, tall building standing separately from the others. Wide double doors lead East into the stables, while to the South, at the other end of the building, is the Smithy. In the upper part of the stables you see the opening of a hayloft with a derrick fixed to the wall beside it.  A rope hangs down from the derrick to the ground.  Also here is a piece of paper, a brass key, an iron key, a metal spike, an altar cloth, a large shield, a silver key, a small knife, a needle, a bronze key, a gold key, a gold disc, a green rod, a crossbow, a glass vial, a saw, a rake, a trowel, a mattock, a gold coin, a screwdriver and the fortress plan.

In Sacristan's Office
You are in a small chamber which was used by the castle sacristan as an office, it is plainly furnished with a simple wooden desk and chair.  Hanging from a rail on the west wall is a curtain.  On the wall next to the desk is a cupboard.

> x cupboard
A simple wooden cupboard with a single door, which does not have a keyhole. You notice a worn patch on the side of the cupboard.

> x side of cupboard
The side of the cupboards has a worn patch near the hinge end, as if it has been frequently touched or hit.

> hit patch
You give the patch on the side of the cupboard a hefty thump with your fist - and the door flies open.

> open cupboard
The cupboard is already open!

> get book
(from the cupboard)
Ok, you take the large book from the cupboard.

> read book
The book is a history of the Teutonic Knights and in the indexes there is a list of former Grand Masters of the Order. The list is quite long, but there are several who the book states are buried in the mausoleum of St. Therese's Chapel, here in the Marienburg Fortress. The book gives a potted biography of each man, and even lists what weapon they were most proficient at using, as follows:

Dietrich von Altenburg: A champion with the broadsword.

Heinrich Dusemer: Was a crack shot with a crossbow.

Konrad von Erlichshausen: His favoured weapon was the rapier.

Konrad von Jungingen: Could wield a battleaxe with amazing dexterity.

Winrich von Kniprode: He was more of an administrator than a warrior, but he did enjoy jousting from a horse with shield and lance.

Michael, Kuchmeister von Sternberg: An all-rounder, proficient with most weapons.

Conrad Zollner von Rothenstein: Reputed to be the world's best Longbowman.

The book also tells you that the Teutonic monastic community was divided into "convents", each headed by a Grand Komtur, and that there was a Home Komtur who dealt with castle administration and provisioning. You also learn that the Komtur commanded "Procurators", who were responsible for court matters and administration of a particular region.

> x book
A large, heavy book with a tooled leather cover, it is entitled "History of the Order of Teutonic Knights".

> draw curtain
You draw the curtain to one side to reveal an alcove.

In Sacristan's Office
You are in a small chamber which was used by the castle sacristan as an office, it is plainly furnished with a simple wooden desk and chair.  The curtain on the wall has been pulled to one side to reveal an alcove you can go West into.  On the wall next to the desk is a cupboard.

St. Therese's Chapel
You are in the nave of St. Therese's Chapel. On the south side of the aisle there is an arched doorway that leads Down into darkness. The exit to the courtyard is to the West.

Looking around, to the left you see a confessional and the main body of the chapel accommodates two blocks of wooden pews divided by the central aisle. The aisle leads to the sanctuary, where the altar, the tabernacle and the sanctuary lamp can be seen. To the right of the sanctuary stands an alcove sheltering a life-size statue of the saint to whom the chapel is dedicated. The whole chapel is embellished with gold and lapis mosaic, and it would normally be lit by hundreds of votive candles placed at the foot of the saint. On the walls to either side of the chapel hang the 14 Stations of the Cross.

You are in the castle granaries, at the south end. This is a cavernous building, large enough to allow whole wagons to be driven in to be loaded and unloaded. On the west side of the building you see a brick-built silo which you can go Up into, there is another at the other end of the granary to the North, while going East leads to the outer bailey.  Also here is a farm wagon.

> push wagon north
You set your shoulder against the wagon and push. It takes some strength, but the wagon rolls to the north end of the granaries.

North End of Granaries
You are at the north end of the castle granaries. This is much the same as the south end, with another brick silo for storing grain which you can go Up into. You can go South, or East outside into the outer bailey. There is also a pair of huge doors beyond the silo which are closed.  Also here is a farm wagon.

> climb wagon
You climb up onto the wagon.

On Wagon
You are standing on the wagon in front of the seat. You are quite high up and the rafters of the granary roof are just above your head. You can Climb Down to the floor of the granary from here, or you could even Jump Down if you were feeling energetic!

> get egg
You can't see any eggs!

> d
You climb down off the wagon to the floor of the granary.

To the north, rising above the mill, you can see the Tetragonal Tower, so-called as it has 10 sides. You can only go South along the granary building, West into the granaries, or North into the mill.  Standing here, blocking your way into the mill, is the ghost of the miller.

South End of NW Bailey

To East and West are paths leading between the curtain wall and the buildings, while going North will take you to the footbridge across the inner moat.
