Alchemist's Laboratory
You are in the Alchemist's laboratory, a round, high-ceilinged chamber near the top of the tower. A wooden staircase winds Up around the wall to a sleeping platform, while to the North there is a large worktable. South you see a large cupboard and the door leads West to the landing.

> u
You move up.

On Sleeping Platform
You are on the Alchemist's sleeping platform, which is home to just a bed and a bedside table. The platform is about 12 feet above the floor of the laboratory and the ceiling is about three feet or so above your head.  Lying on the bed is the Alchemist.

> talk to alchemist
You quietly talk to the alchemist in an effort to wake him up. After the first couple of tries there is no response and you fear he may be dead, but on the third attempt his eyes flutter open. He gasps in fear but you quickly reassure the old man that you mean him no harm. You tell him who you are and why you are here. The alchemist tells you how he fought a duel arcane with Wladyslaw, who proved the stronger.

"The wizard thought he had killed me, but although my wounds are mortal I managed to crawl back here," the alchemist tells you. Feeling that the old man's time is near, you ask him if there is anything you can do for him?

"Yes! There is something you can do for me," the alchemist tells you, hope flaring in his eyes. "You must concoct an elixir which will enable my spirit to enter the netherworld when my body dies. Find me something to write on and I will write down the ingredients."

You search around for something to write on and with, but all you can find is a piece of calfskin and a scrap of charcoal, which you hand to the alchemist. "Most of the ingredients will be found around the fortress," he informs you. "However, the last one may give you a bit of trouble. If my assistant Hans were still alive he would be able to help you, but I fear he perished during the battle. Use the worktable downstairs to make the Elixir on."

You take the calfskin from the alchemist, who sinks back onto his bed with exhaustion. As he falls into a sleep he may not wake up from you hear him whisper, "Do not fail me, Alaric Blackmoon, the success of your mission depends on this!"

> feel under pillow
You slide your hand under the pillow and feel something thin and flat under there. You pull it out gently to avoid waking the alchemist, although he is in such a deep sleep he probably wouldn't wake anyway. What you found under the pillow is a sheet of papyrus.

> d
You move down.

On Top of Ladder

> get broadsword
(from the arm)

> drop sword
You drop the granite broadsword from where you stand at the top of the ladder. Even though you drop it as carefully as you can, as it hits the cobbles of the courtyard it shatters into pieces!

> d

North side of Courtyard(E)
You are on the north side of the Middle Castle Courtyard, where an open archway leads North to steps going down into darkness. Carved into the lintel of the archway are the words "Furnace Vaults". You can also go East, West and SE from here. It is sunny here but the buildings on the east side cast a shadow on the ground.  Here, blocking the archway to the north, is a huge statue of a mounted Teutonic Knight.  The wooden ladder is propped against the statue.  Also here is a piece of paper, a metal spike, a large shield, a lantern, a sheet of parchment, a small knife, a needle, a glass vial, a saw, a rake, a trowel, a mattock, a red crystal, a screwdriver, a broken, granite broadsword, a large book, a bone key, a square of calfskin, a sheet of papyrus, a green crystal, a yellow rod and the fortress plan.

> get all
Ok, you pick up the piece of paper, the metal spike, the large shield, the lantern, the sheet of parchment, the small knife, the needle, the glass vial, the saw, the rake, the trowel, the mattock, the red crystal, the screwdriver, the large book, the bone key, the square of calfskin, the sheet of papyrus, the green crystal, the yellow rod and the fortress plan.  The granite broadsword is shattered into many pieces - you will have to find some way to repair it before you can pick it up again.

> cast reparatur spell at sword
You cast the REPARATUR spell at the broken granite broadsword.

A cloud of green sparkles surrounds the fragments and you watch in amazement as they all move jerkily together. When they are all in their correct position the broadsword glows a bright green and when it fades the sword is whole again.

You place the granite broadsword onto the effigy of the knight.

It shimmers briefly then merges into the stone.  You hear a far-away clash of swords which reverberates softly around the chamber, and then something comes wafting down from the low ceiling of the chamber to rest on the top of the tomb. It is a sheet of vellum.

North End of Footbridge
You are at the north end of the footbridge that leads South to the Middle Castle. Going south will take you onto the drawbridge in front of the Middle Castle gate, which is currently lowered. You can also go North from here into the Lower Castle.

You notice a movement to your right as you reach the end of the footbridge and you look in that direction to see a ghostly figure walk past the main gate coming from the south. As the figure passes the Main Gate it waves to the ghost of the sentry, who waves back in greeting. The figure continues north and walks towards the farmyard. Maybe if you wait by the main gate the ghost will return that way?

The tower is joined to a two-storey building which extends north towards the Hexagonal Tower. To the West you see a farmyard with a couple of buildings to the north & south of it.

You glance at the door to the Armourer's Tower and you notice something different. Then you realise that the wooden sign that had been hanging from the brass knocker is now gone.

> w
You move west.

East end of Farmyard
You are at the east end of the farmyard, where you see a chicken house to the North and a shed to the South. The farmyard extends West and going East will take you to the east side of the Lower Castle.

> n
You move north.

Chicken House
You stand - or rather, stoop, as the roof is quite low - in the chicken house. Here there are dozens of nesting boxes, many containing chickens which eye you warily while others peck at the floor around your feet. The farmyard is South.

> loosen twine
You loosen the twine from around the open end of the bladder.  The gas in the bladder starts to hiss out. You take a sniff and realise from the lack of any odour that it is helium.

> tighten twine
You tighten the twine and the gas stops escaping from the bladder.

> loosen twine
You loosen the twine from around the open end of the bladder.
Gas is still hissing from the bladder.

> inhale gas
You inhale a couple of lungfuls of the gas from the bladder. It is tasteless but you feel your throat tighten slightly.

The pig's bladder is now empty of gas. The twine tied round the open end of the bladder falls off of it.

> sing
You sing to the chickens in your falsetto voice.

The hens start to cluck happily, as if they are singing along with you. After a while your voice starts to deepen into its normal baritone and the chickens start to cluck unhappily, so you stop singing.

> search nests
You search the boxes, feeling gently under the chickens that are nesting in some of them. In one of them you find an egg.

> s
You move south.

Other cupboards and bins for the supplies used by the bakery line the walls. The door leads out West, and a wooden stairway leads Up to a storage area above the main bakery.  Also here is a small hessian sack.

You hear the flutter of wings and a small bird with a forked tail comes flying out from underneath the granary roof. As it arrows over your head you realise it is a swallow. The bird flies out of the granary with a high-pitched "tswitt-tswitt" and is lost to view.

> climb wagon

On Wagon

Furnace Vault
You are in part of the undercroft of the castle where there are furnaces which supplied the hot air which is ducted to the buildings of the Middle Castle. > search vault

Furnace Vault
You are in part of the undercroft of the castle where there are furnaces which supplied the hot air which is ducted to the buildings of the Middle Castle. Opposite the furnaces are empty brick bins which would normally be piled high with the fuel for the furnaces. Stairs lead up to the courtyard from here.  In the shadows at the back of the vault you can see an archway with a wooden door in it.

> kick door
You give the old door a hefty kick with your booted foot - and it collapses outwards, breaking into pieces. You then walk through the archway into another chamber.

On Landing by Stairway
You are standing on a short landing at the top of a steep stairway that goes Down into stygian darkness. The open archway to the furnace vault is West.

> e
There is no route to the east, only west and down.

> d
You walk slowly down the stairway into the darkness. After a few steps you notice the walls of the tunnel you are travelling down are now made of solid stone, indicating that you are now enclosed by the bedrock on which the castle was built. You have to watch your step as some of the stairs have crumbled with age, but after what seems like an eternity you reach the bottom.

Bottom of Stairway
You are at the bottom of the stairway in the catacombs under the castle. A wide tunnel leads East from here, or you can go back Up the stairs.

> e
You move east.

In The Catacombs
You are walking along a long East-West passage in the catacombs. The walls and floor are visible to you, but you cannot see anything else beyond the pool of light that your lantern throws out. The air is very still and you sense that these passageways are extremely ancient.

> e
You move east.

In The Catacombs
You are walking along a long East-West passage in the catacombs. The floor and one wall are visible to you, but you cannot see anything else beyond the pool of light that your lantern throws out. You decide to keep the wall in view as you walk along.

> e
You move east.

In The Catacombs
You are at a junction in the catacombs, where the passage goes East, West and South. The walls and ceiling of the passage can be seen in the light from your lantern and they seem to crowd in on you from the darkness.

You hear the skitter of tiny claws on rock and feel something brush against your boot. There is a brief glimpse of a furry body in the light from your lantern, then it vanishes in the gloom beyond.

> e
You move east.

In The Catacombs
You are in the East-West passage in the catacombs, where the light from your lantern reveals an archway with a closed wooden door in the rock to the North.  On the wall beside the doorway is an old, faded sign which reads: "Custodian of the Catacombs. Private." Next to this is a board with numbered hooks on it.

> put bone key on hook 1
You hang the bone key onto hook number 1. Nothing happens after about a minute, so you take the key off of that hook.

> put bone key on hook 2
You hang the bone key onto hook number 2. Nothing happens after about a minute, so you take the key off of that hook.

> put bone key on hook 3

> put bone key on hook 4
You hang the bone key onto hook number 4. Nothing happens after about a minute, so you take the key off of that hook.

> put bone key on hook 5
You hang the bone key onto hook number 5. Nothing happens after about a minute, so you take the key off of that hook.

> put bone key on hook 6
You hang the bone key onto hook number 6. Nothing happens after about a minute, so you take the key off of that hook.

> put bone key on hook 7
You hang the bone key onto hook number 7.  For a few moments nothing happens, but then you see the key disappear from the hook you hung it on. You hear a loud click that echoes around the passageway and the door next to you opens with a creak of rusty hinges.

> score

> i
You are wearing an amulet, a scrip and your clothes, and you are carrying a piece of paper, a metal spike, a large shield, a lantern, a sheet of parchment, a small knife, a needle, a rope, a small hessian sack, a glass vial, a saw, a rake, a trowel, a mattock, a sheet of vellum, a red crystal, a screwdriver, a large book, a pig's bladder, a small statuette, a square of calfskin, a sheet of papyrus, a swallow's egg, a hen's egg, a green crystal, a broken figurine of a mounted knight, a length of twine and the fortress plan.

> n
You move north.

Custodian's Chamber
You are in a small chamber which must be the living quarters of the Custodian of the Catacombs. It is sparely furnished with a bed and a wooden table and chair. In one wall long shelves have been cut into the rock which contain a surprising number of books, while in the opposite wall there are twelve small niches, eleven of which contain a small statuette.

> put statuette in niche
You place the statuette into the empty niche. As you do so you feel it click into place as if it was magnetised. Suddenly you feel the rock beneath your feet tremble as if massive rocks are grinding together, but it only lasts for a few seconds. You wonder to yourself what that was? Could a secret entrance have opened somewhere in the catacombs?

You hear a noise behind you and turn to see the stooped figure of a ancient old man standing in the doorway, his wizened face has an angered look upon it.

"How dare thee enter my chamber unbidden!" he says angrily. "Get thee gone...." He breaks off as he sees the statuette you have just put into the niche.

"That is my lost statuette, where didst thou find it!?" he asks you, his angry face now one of astonishment. You tell the old man you found it under the alchemist's bed.

"So that is where it was all these years!" He says incredulously. "I remember showing some of the statuettes to my friend the Alchemist, I must have dropped it and it rolled under his bed."

The old man shuffles up to you and looks up into your face. "Who art thou, and how do you come to be in my domain?" You tell him who you are and what has happened in the fortress above ground. "I am the Custodian of the Catacombs. The affairs of the world above are no longer any concern of mine," he tells you, waving his hand in dismissal.

The ancient old man turns to leave the chamber. "You have my gratitude, Duke Alaric," he tells you. "However, I must now return to my duties." He shuffles out of the chamber into the catacombs.

> s
You move south.

In The Catacombs
You are in the East-West passage in the catacombs, where the light from your lantern reveals an archway with an open wooden door leading North into a small chamber.  On the wall beside the doorway is an old, faded sign which reads: "Custodian of the Catacombs. Private." Next to this is a board with numbered hooks on it.  Standing here, leaning on his staff, is the Custodian of the Catacombs.

The Custodian ignores you completely and looks around as if searching for something. He then cocks his head to one side as if listening intently for a sound that you yourself cannot hear.

> ask custodian about statuette
You ask the Custodian of the Catacombs about the statuette that you have returned to him.

"It depicts the ancient goddess Khloris." he tells you. "It was missing for two decades by my reckoning. I thank thee for returning it to me, Duke Alaric."

> ask custodian about khloris
You ask the Custodian about the goddess Khloris.

"She was one of the 12 ancient gods and goddesses of the ancient Pomeranians," he tells you, with a note of reverence in his voice. "Several of them represented the various branches of science and nature, and Khloris was the goddess of Botany."  The Custodian of the Catacombs shuffles off slowly to the east.

You move east.

In The Catacombs
You are at a three-way junction at the end of the long, straight passage in the catacombs which came from the West. You can also go North and SE.  Standing here, leaning on his staff, is the Custodian of the Catacombs.

The Custodian ignores you completely and looks around as if searching for something. He then cocks his head to one side as if listening intently for a sound that you yourself cannot hear.

> ask custodian about rats
You ask the Custodian about the rats you have heard down here and his sombre face takes on a slightly maniacal expression.

"Oh yes, there are lots down here," he enthusiastically tells you. "Big ones too, they do very well on the scraps I feed them".

Your jaw drops in astonishment as he continues. "Would you like one?" he asks. "They make great eating with some fresh vegetables!" With that he reaches into the leather bag he carries over his shoulder and takes something out - it is a dead rat, which he thrusts into your hand.

"There you go, that'll give you some protein," he tells you. As soon as he has said that, his face resumes its sombre expression.

> ask custodian about rat
You ask the Custodian about the rat he has given you.

"A fine example of Rattus Norvegucis," he tells you. "Good eating if you feed them right."  The Custodian of the Catacombs shuffles off slowly to the south-east.

> se
You move southeast.

In The Catacombs
You are following the passage in the catacombs which bends slightly NW and South. The walls are featureless and you cannot see the ceiling at all. From somewhere nearby you hear the sound of trickling water, but you are unable to pinpoint its source.  Standing here, leaning on his staff, is the Custodian of the Catacombs.

You hear a squeak and the sound of small claws skittering away - there are rats down here but the light from your lantern is scaring them away.

The Custodian ignores you completely and looks around as if searching for something. He then cocks his head to one side as if listening intently for a sound that you yourself cannot hear.

Suddenly the Custodian strikes out with his staff at something on the floor of the passageway and you hear a loud squeal and the crunch of bones.

He stoops down, picks something up and puts it into a leather bag he carries over his shoulder.

> ask custodian about staff
You ask the Custodian of the Catacombs about the staff he is carrying.

"It is the badge of office of the Custodians of the Catacombs," he proudly tells you. "It is very ancient, how old I have no idea."

> ask custodian about statuettes
You ask the Custodian of the Catacombs about the statuettes in his chamber.

"They are depictions of the 12 gods of the ancient Pomeranians," he tells you. "The set is complete again, thanks to you."
The Custodian of the Catacombs shuffles off slowly to the south.

In The Catacombs
You have reached a sharp North-West bend in the catacombs. You notice a smooth groove has been worn in the rock of the inside corner of the bend at about waist height, which has been made by the hands of countless people walking past and touching the corner for guidance. A narrower passage goes off towards the SE from here  Standing here, leaning on his staff, is the Custodian of the Catacombs.

You feel a blast of warm air come blowing out of the narrow tunnel to the SE.

The Custodian ignores you completely and looks around as if searching for something. He then cocks his head to one side as if listening intently for a sound that you yourself cannot hear.

> ask custodian about sounds
You ask the Custodian about the sounds he is listening for.

"It's the rats," he tells you. "Can't you hear them talking to one another?"

> ask custodian about bats
You ask the Custodian about the bats you have heard flying about.

"There are two or three varieties in these catacombs" he tells you knowledgeably. "Their meat is very tasty but there isn't much of it, they are just flying mice after all. I prefer the rats, much more meat on them and they are easier to catch - they don't fly!"
The Custodian of the Catacombs shuffles off slowly to the west.

You wait for a while.....and a couple of minutes of time go by without you doing anything.
The Custodian of the Catacombs comes shuffling slowly from the west.

The Custodian ignores you completely and looks around as if searching for something. He then cocks his head to one side as if listening intently for a sound that you yourself cannot hear.

> ask custodian about pumice
You ask the Custodian where you might find some pumice. He looks at you quizzically and thinks for a moment.

"The only place I know of where thee will find that is deep underground. It is some distance from here and the journey is not without its perils." The Custodian frowns at you as if struggling to decide whether to help you or not. After a minute or two he sighs and then speaks.

"As you have restored my lost statuette, I will aid thee, Duke Alaric," the Custodian tells you. "Follow me and do not wander from the path I take."

He shuffles off into the gloom and you follow him closely.

The Custodian leads you further into the catacombs and soon you realise you are heading deep underground. The path is initially along a tortuous passageway which is little more than a well-trodden fissure in the rock.

As you progress you feel the air getting warmer and the rock walls either side of you are indeed warm to the touch. The path you are taking twists and turns, and soon you become disoriented, your natural sense of direction becoming confused.

After about half an hour the passage opens into a vast cavern, filled with gigantic translucent crystal growths which sparkle in the light from your lantern. You stop briefly, mouth agape, to stare at the wondrous formations jutting at all angles from every surface of the cavern.

You are startled out of your reverie by an echoing shout from the Custodian. "Cease thy rubber necking, Duke Alaric, this is no time for sightseeing!"

You hurry to catch up to him and enter another tunnel at the far end of the cavern where you continue descending, the air growing warmer with every step.

Eventually you emerge from the tunnel onto a vast plateau of rock.

By Entrance to Tunnel
You stand at the entrance to the subterranean tunnel which leads back to the catacombs. Your lantern reveals that you are in a huge cleft in the rock, and the roof is only a handful of inches above your head here, but it slopes upwards as the cleft widens. You have no idea of direction down here but ahead you can see what appears to be the edge of the cleft as there is a sharp-edged line against the red glow which comes from below. The edge is about 50 yards away and it would take you only a minute or so to walk to it.  Standing here, leaning on his staff, is the Custodian of the Catacombs.

The Custodian halts by the entrance to the tunnel which led you here and points to the cliff edge some distance away.

"Yonder is the edge of hell, Duke Alaric," the Custodian tells you in a fearful voice. "I will remain here to await thy return." He points to your lantern, saying, "Why doest thou not leave thy lantern with me? It will act as a beacon for thee to walk to when thou hast completed thy task."

You hand over your lantern and the custodian nods his head in salute to you. "Good luck, my lord, I think thou may need it!"

> walk to edge
You walk from the tunnel entrance to the cliff edge.

Edge of Rock Cliff
You are standing at the edge of an underground cliff, overlooking a river of molten lava. The lava flows swiftly about 150 feet below the cliff edge and the glow from it bathes your surrounding in a deep red light. The heat rising from the lava is tremendous and it sucks the moisture from your body. Turning around, you see in the distance the Custodian standing by the tunnel entrance, holding your lantern.

> hammer spike into ground
Holding the spike with one hand and the hammer in the other, you hammer the spike a few centimetres into a fissure in the rock so that it is standing upright. You then grip the hammer in both hands and drive the spike into the fissure so that about 20 cm is left protruding from the ground.

The heat rising from the lava is tremendous and it sucks the moisture from your body. Turning around, you see in the distance the Custodian standing by the tunnel entrance, holding your lantern.   Hammered into the ground about a metre and a half from the cliff is a metal spike.  Looped over this is one end of your rope, the other end of which hangs down over the edge of the cliff.  Also here is a piece of paper, a piece of glass, a large shield, a sheet of parchment, a small knife, a needle, a small hessian sack, a glass vial, a saw, a rake, a trowel, a mattock, a sheet of vellum, a red crystal, a screwdriver, a large book, a pig's bladder, a short piece of wood, a square of calfskin, a sheet of papyrus, a swallow's egg, a hen's egg, a withered rose, a green crystal, a broken figurine of a mounted knight, a length of twine, a large hammer, a chainmail haubergeon and the fortress plan.

As you breathe a sigh of relief that you have got the pumice, you hear a loud crack and feel the rock under your feet shudder ominously. You leap away from the cliff edge just in the nick of time as about a metre or two of the rock collapses and falls into the lava river, taking your climbing equipment with it! Hammering that spike into the fissure must have weakened the rock - you are very lucky it didn't collapse while you were climbing on the rope!

Edge of Rock Cliff
You are standing at the edge of an underground cliff, overlooking a river of molten lava. The lava flows swiftly about 150 feet below the cliff edge and the glow from it bathes your surrounding in a deep red light. The heat rising from the lava is tremendous and it sucks the moisture from your body. Turning around, you see in the distance the Custodian standing by the tunnel entrance, holding your lantern. Part of the cliff edge has collapsed, making the edge a yard or so narrower than it was.  Also here is a piece of paper, a piece of glass, a large shield, a sheet of parchment, a small knife, a needle, a small hessian sack, a glass vial, a saw, a rake, a trowel, a mattock, a sheet of vellum, a red crystal, a screwdriver, a large book, a pig's bladder, a short piece of wood, a square of calfskin, a sheet of papyrus, a swallow's egg, a hen's egg, a withered rose, a green crystal, a broken figurine of a mounted knight, a length of twine, a chainmail haubergeon and the fortress plan.

> get all
Ok, you pick up the piece of paper, the piece of glass, the large shield, the sheet of parchment, the small knife, the needle, the small hessian sack, the glass vial, the saw, the rake, the trowel, the mattock, the sheet of vellum, the red crystal, the screwdriver, the large book, the pig's bladder, the short piece of wood, the square of calfskin, the sheet of papyrus, the swallow's egg, the hen's egg, the withered rose, the green crystal, the broken figurine of a mounted knight, the length of twine, the chainmail haubergeon and the fortress plan.

> walk to tunnel
You walk back to where the Custodian is waiting for you.

By Entrance to Tunnel
You stand at the entrance to the subterranean tunnel which leads back to the catacombs. Your lantern reveals that you are in a huge cleft in the rock, and the roof is only a handful of inches above your head here, but it slopes upwards as the cleft widens. You have no idea of direction down here but ahead you can see what appears to be the edge of the cleft as there is a sharp-edged line against the red glow which comes from below. The edge is about 50 yards away and it would take you only a minute or so to walk to it.  Standing here, leaning on his staff, is the Custodian of the Catacombs.

You take the lump of pumice from your scrip and triumphantly show it to the Custodian.

"Well done, Duke Alaric," he tells you. "I knew thou couldst succeed!"

The old man returns your lantern to you and he points to the tunnel.

"We must now return to the catacombs. Please keep up - and no rubber-necking!"

The custodian sets off along the tunnel, with you following behind. The journey is uneventful and, despite his warning, you cannot help but gaze about you as the two of you traverse the cavern of crystals.

Eventually you reach the catacombs and the Custodian leads you to the passageway that leads to the stairway.

In The Catacombs
You are at a junction in the catacombs, where the passage goes East, West and South. The walls and ceiling of the passage can be seen in the light from your lantern and they seem to crowd in on you from the darkness.  Standing here, leaning on his staff, is the Custodian of the Catacombs.

The Custodian turns to you and says, "I must now return to my duties, Duke Alaric. I wish thee every success with the rest of thy quest!"

You thank the old man for his help. "No matter, no matter," he says as he shuffles off to resume his patrol. "Thou only needs to ask if thee needs further aide."

The Custodian shuffles off east along the passageway into the stygian darkness.

In The Catacombs

In The Catacombs
This part of the catacombs runs North and East and you notice there is a slight upward slope to the north. A much narrower passage leads off to the SW.

> sw
You move southwest.

In The Catacombs
You are in a narrow part of the passageway, you could reach out with your arms and easily touch the walls either side of you. The roof of the passage is very low and you find yourself ducking to avoid grazing the top of your head. The passage bends in an arc to NE and SE.

> se
You move southeast.

In The Catacombs
This part of the passageway in the catacombs has a ceiling so low that you have to be careful you don't hit your head. It runs NW and East and an opening in the rock leads NE into a rock chamber.  Another very narrow fissure has opened in the South wall of the passageway.

> s
You move south.

In Narrow Fissure
You are squeezed sideways into a narrow fissure in the rock. You can go North back to the passageway or further South into the fissure.

> s
You move south.

Near end of Fissure
You are in the fissure in the rock, where it widens out so that you can walk properly. A weird moaning sound comes from the South, and you can also go North back into the narrow part of the fissure.

> s
You move south.

On Rock Ledge
The fissure has opened onto a narrow rock ledge, which is only a yard or so wide. You cannot see anything beyond the light cast by your lantern except for what appears to be the flat top of a pinnacle poking up out of the darkness about 3 metres to the south. You guess that you are standing in a vast cavern above a vast subterranean abyss, at the bottom of which must be a body of water - maybe a subterranean lake, judging by the damp wind that blows up from the depths, source of the moaning noise you could hear from the fissure.

> cast wieder spell at wood
You recite the words of the incantation at the piece of wood. It is suddenly surrounded by a scintillating cloud of red sparkles and it then grows in size and length until it is restored to its former size.

Far Side of Abyss
You stand on the far side of the abyss, where a few jagged stones are all that remain of the footbridge. You sense that something lies beyond the pool of light cast by your lantern, but here it only illuminates a large, ancient, marble altar which glows like a beacon several yards to the South. Otherwise, you can see nothing at all and, apart from the pinnacle to the North, you have no idea what lies beyond. The wind from the abyss seems stronger here and you can also hear the sound of water flowing from the depths below.  The plank spans the abyss across to the pinnacle.

> s
You move south.

By Altar
You are standing by the altar, which almost glows in the light emitted by your lantern. You cannot see it, but you know that the abyss you crossed to get here is several yards to the North in the utter darkness beyond the pool of bright light that you stand in. You notice that it is calm here, none of the wind from the abyss reaching where you stand.

> get withered rose from scrip
You take the withered rose from the scrip.

> put rose on altar
You put the withered rose onto the gleaming, marble altar.

> pray to khloris
You say a prayer to Khloris, goddess of botany. The air around you is suddenly filled with the heady fragrance of many different flowers, and you see the vague figure of a woman take shape on the other side of the altar. She reaches down and touches the withered rose, which is transformed into a beautiful rose, as if fresh from the bush.

You hear a woman's voice whisper in your mind, "This rose will never die, Duke Alaric," the goddess tells you. "Nor will its fragrance ever fade, it is unique among flowers."

The shape then fades away, as does the scent of flowers.

> get rose
(from the gleaming, marble altar)

> n
You go to walk across the plank but you are stopped in your tracks by an unseen force. From out of the darkness in front of you the ghost of the gardener approaches and stops in front of you.

The ghost of the gardener holds his hand out towards you. "Please return my rose to me, Duke Alaric," he pleads. "I spent many a long hour nurturing that rosebush and I may only rest if I can touch and smell its last bloom once again.

The ghost looks at you with such a sad face that you would only be too glad to return his rose to him. However, you know that if you do you will lose it forever - maybe you can think of a way to make the gardener happy and keep the rose for yourself?

> cast verdopplung spell at rose
You cast the verdopplung spell at the eternal rose, being careful to pronounce the words of the incantation correctly. A cloud of scintillating green sparkles briefly surrounds the rose and as the sparkles fade you see that an exact duplicate of the rose sits beside the real rose.

You pick up the real rose first, putting it in your scrip. You then pick up the duplicate rose and turn to face the ghost of the gardener. You walk towards him and place the rose onto the palm of his outstretched hand.

His craggy face breaks into a big grin and he raises the rose to his nose and inhales its wonderful perfume.

"Thank you, Duke Alaric, I will be grateful to you for all of eternity," he tells you as he gazes in adoration at the rose.

He turns and walks towards the abyss and you are amazed to see a ghostly vision of the footbridge that once spanned the abyss appear in the gloom. As the ghost walks onto the footbridge and disappears into the darkness, so does the image of the bridge.

You move northwest.

In The Catacombs
You are in a narrow part of the passageway, you could reach out with your arms and easily touch the walls either side of you. The roof of the passage is very low and you find yourself ducking to avoid grazing the top of your head. The passage bends in an arc to NE and SE.

> ne
You move northeast.

In The Catacombs
This part of the catacombs runs North and East and you notice there is a slight upward slope to the north. A much narrower passage leads off to the SW.  Standing here, leaning on his staff, is the Custodian of the Catacombs.

The Custodian ignores you completely and looks around at the walls, floor and roof of this part of the catacombs as if searching for something.

> ask custodian for rat
You ask the Custodian for another dead rat.

"Have you eaten the one I gave you already?" he asks you. "I said you would enjoy it."

He opens the flap of his shoulder bag, takes a rat out and hands it to you.

"There you go, plenty more where that came from," he tells you.

> ask custodian for dead rat
"I have already given you a rat," the Custodian says to you. "Don't be greedy!"  The Custodian of the Catacombs shuffles off slowly to the south-west.

Cloisters North (Middle)
You are in the cloisters, just south of the north end. By the inside wall here, facing the courtyard, is a wooden bench. You can go North or South.  Sitting on the wooden bench here is the ghost of a young man.

> get calfskin from scrip
You take the square of calfskin from the scrip.

> get rose from scrip
You take the eternal rose from the scrip.

> talk to hans
You talk to the ghost of the young man, telling him who you are. He tells you his name is Hans.

"Oh what am I to do, Duke Alaric," Hans asks you, gazing adoringly at the young woman sitting at the other end of the cloister. "I know that Grizelda loves me, but I have nothing of beauty to give her to prove it. Can you help me?"

> speak to hans
You have already spoken to the young man and he has told you about his love for Grizelda.

> greet hans
I don't understand what you want to do with The ghost of a young man.

> show calfskin to hans
You show the calfskin to the young man, who takes it from you.

"This is my master's handwriting!" he exclaims. He reads the recipe for the elixir and a sly look appears briefly on his face.

"Tell you what," he says to you. "You bring me something of beauty that I can give to Grizelda and I will tell you what equipment you will need to make this elixir!"

He gives you back the calfskin and just sits there gazing wistfully at his love at the other end of the cloister.

> give calfskin to hans
"I told you," Hans says to you. "Bring me something beautiful and I will tell you what equipment you need."

> show rose to hans
You show the eternal rose to Hans, who gets to his feet, takes it from you and looks at it in amazement.

"That is truly a wonderful thing to behold," he says in an awe-struck voice. "Its beauty is a fitting tribute to Grizelda."

Hans stands up and as if by magic the calfskin appears in his hand. He conjures a quill from thin air and writes some words on the calfskin, then hands it to you. He then walks down the cloister and goes to bended knee in front of Grizelda. He offers her the rose and she demurely takes it from him. What passes between them is left unsaid as the young lovers rise to their feet and embrace.

With joy written all over their faces, they walk arm-in-arm towards you. As they reach you they solemnly nod to you and, as they pass by, fading from view, Hans gives you a huge smile and a wink before they disappear from view.

> remove gauntlet
Ok, you remove the leather gauntlet.

> make elixir
Following the Alchemist's instructions to the letter, you mix together the saxifrage petals, the egg yolk and the swallow's eggshell with the water in the retort, which you heat on the furnace for 10 minutes. You notice the eggshell dissolves in the water as it warms up.  You grind the lump of pumice in the mortar using the pestle and you add that to the mixture,and then you heat the final mixture for another 15 minutes. The liquid thickens slightly and turns a brilliant lime-green in colour.

At the end of the 15 minutes you take the retort off the furnace and allow it to cool. During this time, the burning sacking is finally consumed, leaving just some ashes inside the furnace. The Elixir is now ready to give to the Alchemist once you have found a more suitable vessel to pour it into - the Alchemist will not be able to drink properly from the retort!

> pour elixir into flagon
Your pour the elixir from the retort into the glass flagon.

Alchemist's Laboratory
You are in the Alchemist's laboratory, a round, high-ceilinged chamber near the top of the tower. A wooden staircase winds Up around the wall to a sleeping platform, while to the North there is a large worktable. South you see a large cupboard and the door leads West to the landing.

> u
You move up.

On Sleeping Platform
You are on the Alchemist's sleeping platform, which is home to just a bed and a bedside table. The platform is about 12 feet above the floor of the laboratory and the ceiling is about three feet or so above your head.  Lying on the bed is the Alchemist.

> wake alchemist
You gently shake the alchemist's shoulder to wake him up again. His eyes open, he sees the glass flagon with the Elixir in it and he manages to smile weakly.

"I am amazed, Duke Alaric, you have succeeded!" the Alchemist whispers in a frail voice. "Quickly, for I feel that my time is nigh, you will have to hold the flagon to my lips, I have no strength left."

You put one hand under the old man's shoulders and raise him up a little, then you hold the flagon to his lips and tip it up. He slowly drinks the Elixir down, coughing once or twice.

When he has drunk all of it, you lay him back down again. His hand suddenly reaches up to grab the front of your jacket and he pulls your face close to his with the last bit of strength left in his grievously wounded body.

"I will help you where I was unable to help myself, Duke Alaric," the old man tells you. He reaches up and takes your amulet in his hand and whispers the incantation of a magic spell. The amulet glows briefly and the Alchemist releases it.

"I have set a ward on your amulet that will protect you from the kind of magic Wladyslaw will use to kill you. Had I known beforehand I could have protected myself."

The old man's eyes go wide as his breathing gets more ragged.

"Beware Wladyslaw, the closer you get to him, the more he is likely to break the rules!" He releases your jacket and he lays back with a deep sigh.

His body begins to fade and his face smiles at you. As he disappears from view you catch the faint aroma of almonds once again.

Komtur's Office
You are in the Komtur's Office, which is plainly decorated and furnished with a large desk behind which is a high-backed wooden chair. There is a door behind the desk in the North wall. The hallway is South.  The ghost of the komtur is sitting in the chair, gazing at the figurine of a bird on his desk.

Sitting in the chair behind the desk is the ghostly figure of a very distinguished-looking man. He tears his eyes away from the figurine of a bird on his desk and looks at you questioningly.

"Good day to you, my good fellow," he says welcomingly. "I can see that you are not one of Wladyslaw's men. Who are you and what do you disturb my thoughts with?"

> talk to komtur
You introduce yourself to the ghost of the Komtur and tell him your purpose in being here. His eyebrow goes up at your mention of your name.

"Your reputation precedes you, Duke Alaric," he tells you. "Finding the Fist of Fire was a great achievement. My name is Werner von Orselen and in life I was the Komtur of this fortress. I can aid you in a small way, but first you must give me back the thing I treasured the most in life," he says, indicating the bird on his desk.

> ask komtur about bird
You ask the Komtur about his Gyrfalcon.

"Her name is Tiercel and she is a white Gyrfalcon," the Komtur tells you. "I myself travelled many leagues to Valkenswaard in The Netherlands to bid for her in the annual falconry auctions. She cost me a king's ransom, but she was worth it. When the castle was attacked the falconer released all the birds to prevent them being captured by Wladyslaw's troops - they probably would have killed and eaten them!" He looks at the figurine wistfully. "The falconer carved and painted that, it is all I have to remind me of her beauty."

It is a large, magnificent, fan-vaulted room with several columns that support the ceiling and wooden parquet flooring with vents in various places which allow hot air from the furnace vault to warm the room in winter. The tables and benches that populate the refectory have been pushed and piled against the wall next to the wide arched doorway that leads out North. Another doorway leads South to a staircase that leads up to the upper floors and, behind a wooden screen on the East side of the refectory, a double doorway leads to the kitchen. The only other piece of furniture in the refectory is a large metal locker standing against one wall.  Also here is a miniature cannon.

> show gauntlet to falconer
You show the gauntlet to the ghost of the falconer, who takes it from you and smiles.

"Thank you, Duke Alaric," The falconer tells you, sliding his hand into the gauntlet and flexing the fingers. "I can now try to coax Tiercel down from the sky."

He turns and walks away into the garden area. You watch from the corner of the wall and see the falconer standing by the mews, looking up at the sky. He then reaches into a pouch tied to his belt and takes out something, which he then holds above his head.

He whistles in a special way a couple of times and calls the name "Tiercel". Suddenly a white bird of prey swoops down from out of the sky and perches on top of the curtain wall surrounding the garden and sits there looking down at him.

The falconer drops his hands to his sides then swings them out again to bring them back up above his head once more. You realise he is using a gesture the bird may be trained to respond to. The bird is obviously very wary and will not come down.

You look at what the falconer is holding and realise that it is a dead rat. Hunger overcomes the bird's wariness and it launches itself off the wall and comes swooping down to snatch the rat out of the falconer's hands. The bird flies up to perch on the top of the mews and gobbles the rat down. The falconer stretches his gauntleted hand out to the side of him and calls the bird by name - "Tiercel" - a couple of times.

The bird flies down and is about to land on the falconer's gauntlet, but it sees you and veers off, arrowing up into the sky and out of sight. He calls Tiercel again, but the bird does not respond. He looks around, sees you standing there and he walks over to you with a resigned expression on his ghostly face.

"I had almost got her down that time," he says, wearily. He pulls the gauntlet off his hand and drops it onto the ground at your feet. "You have a go," he tells you. "You might have a bit more luck than me!"

The falconer walks off towards the mews, fading from view as he goes.....

He turns to the worktable behind him, picks up the leather hood and turns back to hand it to you.

"If you could please ask the Komtur to stop Tiercel from clawing at the laces, I would be grateful. That is the third time I have had to repair them."

The ghost nods in farewell, turns around and walks away, fading from view as he goes.

Komtur's Office
You are in the Komtur's Office, which is plainly decorated and furnished with a large desk behind which is a high-backed wooden chair. There is a door behind the desk in the North wall. The hallway is South.  The ghost of the komtur is sitting in the chair, gazing at the figurine of a bird on his desk.

You walk into the Komtur's office with Tiercel on your arm. At first he does not notice her but she makes a small "Chup!" sound and his head jerks up and his mouth drops open in astonishment.

"You have found her!" the Komtur says, joyously. He gets to his feet and holds his arm out to her. You wonder how the bird is going to sit on the ethereal limb when, to your utter amazement, the falcon's form starts to fade and her weight on your arm disappears, as does the leather gauntlet, which magically appears on the Komtur's outstretched arm. Tiercel's now ghostly form hops onto the Komtur's gauntleted hand and he strokes her breast in welcome, crooning to her in low tones.

The Komtur looks at you with gratitude in his eyes. "My thanks, Duke Alaric," he says, and points to the door in the North wall. "You may now continue your mission, through that door is a travel portal, which you can use to travel to other places. I wish you the best of luck, but beware that you might find peril if you use the portal."

With that he walks towards the door to the hallway. "Come, my beauty," he says to Tiercel. "Let us fly!" As he walks out of the door, his form and that of the falcon on his arm fade from view.

> look south
You peep around the curtain and see a chapel with about 20 knights chatting quietly while they wait for the priest to arrive to start mass.

You hear a hush descend on the chapel as the priest enters. You expect him to start the service by speaking the Latin words of the sign of the cross, but instead he speaks to the knights.

"A carrier pigeon has just arrived from Konigsberg with an urgent message about our brothers in Toompea," he tells them. "The castle is under siege by the Sambians and we will be riding to their aid as soon as we can. Our brothers at Konigsberg are also on their way. After this service you should report to your units. Beware that the Sambians are rumoured to have captured a travel portal amulet - treat any strangers seen emerging from a travel portal as hostile, they are to be apprehended for interrogation if possible."

There is a brief buzz of conversation as the knights discuss the news, then silence again as the priest starts the mass. You sigh as you realise that they may be there for some time.

You also realise that you now cannot ask these knights for help with your quest! If you emerge from this portal they are going to think you are a Sambian infiltrator and you will be arrested. The same might happen if you go anywhere else using the amulet - maybe you should go somewhere else for now, you can come back here when the service is over?

The Marshal's office is West and you can also go North, South, East, NE and SE. The courtyard is a heaving mass of knights, esquires, horses and baggage wagons, with more knights joining the throng as they finish their preparations for the journey to Toompea. The noise is incredible and the smell of horses and horse dung fill the air with a miasma of pungency. A light drizzle is falling, which is helping to keep the dust down.

> look around
The courtyard is a seething mass of men, horses and baggage wagons. The noise and smell are incredible as the knights and their men prepare to march to the relief of Toompea. You notice, however, that the NW corner of the courtyard, a few metres to the North, is relatively clear of horses and men.

> n
You move north.

NW of Courtyard
You stand in the northwest corner of the courtyard. It is relatively clear here, the press of knights and horses being further southeast. You had better not tarry too long as you do not want to arouse suspicion.

> look around

North Side of Courtyard
You stand on the north side of the courtyard which extends East, West, South, SE and SW from here, although access to these areas would be difficult because of the sheer mass of men, horses and wagons filling the courtyard. Just a few yards from where you stand there are two large sliding doors on the building here.

You see a couple of men come out of a small door in the building a bit further east. They yell at everyone to clear a space, and the knights in the way reluctantly move their equipment, horses and wagons away from the area. They then pull open two great sliding doors, which part to reveal a large opening leading north into the building. The men run inside and moments later a pair of horses, with one of them being ridden by a knight, come walking out of the opening pulling a large cannon. They pull the cannon towards the centre of the courtyard, scattering knights and horses, all of whom protest vehemently. The rider stops the horses and turns to look at the opening, as if expecting something else to come out.

Maybe you should stay here to see what is about to come out of the building.

North Side of Courtyard
You stand on the north side of the courtyard which extends East, West, South, SE and SW from here, although access to these areas would be difficult because of the sheer mass of men, horses and wagons filling the courtyard. Just a few yards from where you stand there is a wide opening leading North, where it is very dark and you cannot see what purpose the building serves without going inside. Both doors either side of the opening are open.   Here you see a horse-drawn cannon.

> z
You wait for a while.....and a couple of minutes of time go by without you doing anything.

You hear neighing and the steely clip-clop of hooves and then the horse-drawn cannon moves off towards the middle of the courtyard and another team of horses pulls a wagon out of the building to the north. The driver stops the horses, jumps down from the wagon, and goes to one of the horses to adjust its harness. You notice that the tarpaulin covering the wagon is loose.

> x wagon
An ordinary four-wheeled cargo wagon, it is being towed by a team of four cart horses. The cargo in the back of the wagon is covered by a large tarpaulin.

> lift tarpaulin
You lift up the tarpaulin and look under it. The wagon is carrying the munitions for the cannon and you can see cannonballs, wads and gunpowder cartridges as well as other items you cannot identify.

> get cartridge
(from the horse-drawn wagon)
You reach into the wagon and take out a powder cartridge.

Maybe you should not let anyone see that you have taken it!

The wagon driver, having finished adjusting the horse's harness, jumps back onto the wagon, grabs the reins and flicks them onto the backs of his team. As the wagon trundles forward to join the cannon team waiting in the middle of the courtyard, the doors are pushed shut from inside the building.

North Side of Courtyard
You stand on the north side of the courtyard which extends East, West, South, SE and SW from here, although access to these areas would be difficult because of the sheer mass of men, horses and wagons filling the courtyard. The sliding doors to the building here have now been closed and you can just about see the cannon and its munitions wagon to the south near the centre of the courtyard. The area around them seethes with activity as the knights, both mounted and on foot, prepare to leave the castle for Toompea.

> put cartridge in sleeve
You put the cartridge in the sleeve of the habit so that no-one can see it.

There doesn't seem to be anything else here that might be of use, so you had better get back to Marienburg before someone spots you!

> fahren lubeck

Travel Portal (Lubeck)
You stand in the curtained-off alcove that is the transfer portal next to the Chapel in the Cathedral in Lubeck. You can go South into the chapel itself.

As your vision clears you become aware of a voice chanting a benediction coming from the chapel beyond the curtain. You should wait, however, until the coast is clear!

> listen
You hear the priest say the final words of the mass, "Dóminus vobíscum," to which the knights reply, "Et cum spíritu tuo." The priest then gives the final dismissal of "Ite, missa est." There is a momentary silence and then you hear much shuffling of booted feet and muted conversation as the mass celebrants file out of the chapel. You hear the priest say to someone, "Leave those there, the sacristan can put them away later." Then there is silence in the chapel, although you can hear the muted hum of scores of voices coming from the cathedral beyond.

> look around curtain
You peep around the curtain and see that the chapel is now empty.

Marienkirche (Rostock)
You stand in the Marienkirche in Rostock. The High Altar is to your right, behind which, further to the East on the apse of the church, is the Astronomical Clock. The side chapel is to the South, while the main doors of the church lead West to the street outside. The aisle is full of worshippers arriving for a mass and over by the side of the High Altar, you see a group of clergymen and high-ranking knights. The way East to the clock is closed off by a barrier upon which is a sign: "No Entry - Work in Progress".

> distribute hymnals

Apse behind Altar
You are in the apse behind the High Altar, standing in front of the Astronomical Clock. You can only go West from here, but a barrier separates the apse from the rest of the church. A trestle table has be set up here and on it you see parts of the clock that have been removed for repair.  The clockmaker is here.

> talk to clockmaker
You ask the clockmaker what he is doing. He is obviously busy, but glad someone is taking an interest in what he is doing.

"The astronomical clock was damaged during reconstruction work on the cathedral a few months ago," he tells you. "The mechanisms are extremely delicate and easily broken. Now, if you'll excuse me, I have work to do."

You thank the clockmaker for taking the time to speak to you and he returns to his work.

> x clock
The clock is an enormous piece of mechanical wizardry. There are dials showing the phases of the moon, the zodiacal constellations, month of the year. You believe it also tells the time!

At the base of the clock is a whole load of pieces of the inner workings of one of the dials which the clockmaker has removed from the clock.

> ask clockmaker about clock
You ask the clockmaker about the clock. He pauses in his work to talk to you.

"The clock was built over 100 years ago by my ancestor Hans Duringer, who originally came from Nuremberg," he tells you proudly. He points up at the highest dial.

"The top dial gives an hourly performance of the apostles crossing before Jesus for a blessing before entry into eternal bliss, but the last, Judas, is shut out. The middle dial comprises a clock with daily time, zodiac, moon phases, and month. Lastly, the bottom dial is a calendar, which will give the date until the year 2017."

You thank the clockmaker for the information and he returns to his work. You wonder to yourself what the world will be like in 2017 - will it be a better place?

> ask clockmaker about dials
"I have already explained about the dials," the clockmaker says to you. "Please allow me to continue my work."

> ask clockmaker about mechanism
You ask the clockmaker about the mechanism of the clock. He pauses in his work to talk to you.

"The mechanism was constructed over 100 years ago by my ancestor Hans Duringer, who originally came from Nuremberg," he tells you proudly. "It is extremely complicated and I have devoted my whole life to learning how the various mechanisms works and how to repair them if they go wrong."

> ask clockmaker about rods
What rods?

> x rods
What rods?

> x workings
These are various sections and parts of the astronomical clock that have been removed so that the clockmaker can work on them. Amongst them you see some metal rods.

> get rod
You take just one of the rods.

North Battlements
You are on the north battlements of Toompea castle, outside the guardroom which is the only structure on this part of the battlements. These extend to the East and West of you, in which direction you see a tall, cylindrical tower soaring many feet into the sky. At the eastern end is another tower, this one much lower. The battlements are crowded with knights, armed to the teeth, they all brandish their weapons and scream insults over the crenellations at the hordes of their Sambian besiegers, which swarm up the hill upon which the castle is built. You can go East to a smaller tower, West along the battlements towards the tall tower, or South back inside the guardroom.

As you are looking around at the mayhem that surrounds you, a flight of arrows fired by Sambian archers below the castle come arcing over the crenellations. A couple of knights are hit and they stagger back, either dead or wounded. One of the arrows plunges down over the top of your shield and hits your chest! Fortunately it fails to penetrate your chainmail and the arrow clatters harmlessly on the stones at your feet.

West End of Battlements
You stand at the western end of the battlements, above you the tower soars into the sky. An open archway leads West into the tower and the battlements extend East. Above the archway you see the inscription "Hermann Tower". There are fewer knights here, but like their fellows further along the battlements they are goading the Sambian besiegers with insults and waving their weapons at them. Here and there, archers rain arrows down upon their foe.

You duck as a large rock comes hurtling over the battlements from below. It shatters into pieces against a wall a few metres away and luckily nobody is hurt by it.

> w
You go to enter the tower, but are bowled over by a huge Sambian warrior who comes charging out of the doorway leading a raiding party who have infiltrated the castle. You fall backwards onto the hard stones as the Sambian soldiers come boiling out of the tower. A shout goes up from the knights as they all rush towards the invaders and fall upon them with their weapons.

The Sambian warrior who knocked you down is wielding a huge battleaxe with amazing strength, cutting down knights all around him. They fall back under the onslaught and the warrior spots you sprawled on the floor. He raises his axe and brings it down upon you.

You hold your shield above you at arms length to protect yourself and as the warrior brings his axe down it hits the shield with a bone-jarring crash, but it is deflected away from you. You kick out at the warrior, who trips over your outstretched legs and goes sprawling onto the floor. He tries to get to his feet but several knights quickly fall upon him and he is hacked down.

> show calfskin to herbalist
You show the calfskin to the herbalist, who takes it and reads the words written on it.

"Hmmm, this would appear to be the formula for an elixir of some kind." He ponders for a while before speaking again. "Well, the saxifrage is a small plant that grows in rocky crevices, the 'impure carbon'...could be the residue from a fire - soot? Hen's egg from the farmyard, easy enough. Swallow's egg - you might have some luck there, it's their nesting season."

His eyebrows go up when he sees the last ingredient.

"Powdered pumice! Pumice is solidified lava. The nearest volcano is not that far from here, but it has been dormant for hundreds of years."

He hands the calfskin back to you and carries on with his weeding.

> put black rod in se hole

Mausoleum - SE Passageway
You are at the end of the passageway that went SE from the central chamber of the mausoleum. There is a metal gate here, beyond which you can see a small chamber with a tomb in it.  On the wall next to the gate there is a metal lever.

> pull lever
You pull on the lever, which only moves a few centimetres. There is a loud metallic click and the gate swings open with a creak of rusty hinges.

> se

Mausoleum - SE Chamber
You stand in a small chamber in the mausoleum, where a tomb takes up most of the space on the floor, there is barely enough room to walk around it. The passageway leading to the central chamber of the mausoleum is to the NW.

> untie bowstring
You untie the bowstring from around the lodestone.

> restring longbow
Bracing one end of the bow on the ground against your boot, you pull down on the other end with all your strength in your right arm. You manage to bend the bow enough to slip the knot at the end of the bowstring over the nock and the longbow is ready for use.

> put longbow on tomb
You place the longbow on the tomb. Nothing happens for a second or two then you watch as the longbow merges with the figure of the knight on the tomb.

> put arrow on tomb
You place the arrow on the tomb. Nothing happens for a second or two then you see the arrow merge with the figure of the knight on the tomb.

You hear a far-away clash of swords which reverberates softly around the chamber, then you smile when - as you expected - an object starts to rise out of the figure on the tomb - it is a metal rod.

You hear a far-away clash of swords which reverberates softly around the chamber, then you wait for something to happen, but nothing apparently does. Then you hear a loud grinding crack and the floor of the tomb jerks under your feet as if rock has suddenly split apart.

Middle of MC Courtyard

The cannon is already aimed at the wall under the gatehouse.

> drop all
Ok, you put down the piece of glass, the large shield, the lantern, the besom, the small knife, the needle, the glass vial, the saw, the rake, the trowel, the mattock, the lodestone, the screwdriver, the large book, the pig's bladder, the glass retort, the ceramic furnace, the square of calfskin, the black cannonball, the monk's habit, the cartridge, the linstock, the length of twine, the glass flagon, the metal candlestick, the padlock keys, the metal key, the dirty wad, the leather flask and the fortress plan.

> load cannon
You load the cartridge, then the cannonball and finally the wad into the muzzle of the cannon. Then, using the besom as a makeshift ramrod, you ram the charge firmly down to the breech end of the cannon.

> get flask
Ok, you pick up the leather flask.

> pour primer in hole
You pour some gunpowder from the flask into the hole in the top of the barrel. The cannon is now ready to fire.

> drop flask
Ok, you put down the leather flask.

> get glass
Ok, you pick up the piece of glass.

> focus sunlight on slowmatch
You focus the rays of the sun onto the end of the slowmatch and after a few seconds it bursts into flame and starts to burn slowly.

> drop glass
Ok, you put down the piece of glass.

> get linstock
Ok, you pick up the linstock.

> fire cannon
Standing to one side of the breech end of the cannon, you reach out with the linstock and touch the lit end of the slowmatch to the priming hole in the top of the barrel. There is a puff of white smoke as the priming gunpowder ignites, then....

B - O - O - O - M!

The cannon fires with a tremendous bang and a huge cloud of white smoke. A second afterwards you hear a loud crash as the cannonball hits the wall followed by another loud thud as the ball hits something else beyond. Then there is silence.

> get all
Ok, you pick up the piece of glass, the large shield, the lantern, the besom, the small knife, the needle, the glass vial, the saw, the rake, the trowel, the mattock, the lodestone, the screwdriver, the large book, the pig's bladder, the glass retort, the ceramic furnace, the square of calfskin, the monk's habit, the length of twine, the glass flagon, the metal candlestick, the padlock keys, the metal key, the leather flask and the fortress plan.  The cannon is far too large for you to pick up!

> score
You have scored 1351 points out of 1500, after taking 1945 turns.

You hear a exclamation of "Good heavens!" behind you and turn to see the ghost of the herbalist walking towards you.

"I wondered what all the noise was about," he says, pointing at the hole you have made in the granite wall. "I thought it was thunder, but now I see it was you. Quite a hole you've made there!"

He rubs his hands together to brush the dirt off of them. "I've finished weeding my herb beds," he tells you happily. "Thanks for the use of the hoe, I've returned it to the shed in the farmyard."

With that, he walks away towards the north side of the courtyard, fading from view as he goes.

> fire cannon
You have fired the cannon once, you cannot do it a second time.

> score
You have scored 1351 points out of 1500, after taking 1947 turns.

> bend bars

> get henbane
You push your arm into the widened gap you made in the bars and grab a handful of the Henbane.

Suddenly the hair on the back of your neck stands on end as your hear a ghostly voice whisper by your ear.

"Be very careful, the henbane is very poisonous," the voice warns you. "So don't eat any part of the plants if you value your life!" You realise that the voice is that of the Alchemist!

NW Corner of Courtyard
You are in the NW corner of the High Castle Courtyard, by the tunnel under the buildings that leads North to the bridge to the Middle Castle. The courtyard, the floor of which is entirely cobbled, extends East, South and SE, in which direction is a large well. You can also go West into a cloister that runs most of the way around the courtyard at the bottom of the castle buildings.

As you enter the courtyard of the High Castle, you immediately see that it is much smaller than the Middle Castle, only about 30 metres square. The dominant feature of the courtyard is a large covered well in the centre, behind which, on the southern side, a large tree grows.

The buildings of the High Castle are very tall, four stories high, casting most of the courtyard in shadow, and above the cloisters that runs nearly the whole way around the courtyard is a galleried level with large windows with open stone tracery that look out over the square. Soaring over the square in the NE corner is the Bell Tower, which you must gain access to after - or rather IF - you defeat Wladyslaw.

You repress a shudder as you realise that your foe must be somewhere in this complex of buildings, waiting for you to find him. You then recall the alchemist's words that the sorcerer-prince is not to be trusted.....

There are four soldiers in the corridor, one seated behind a desk facing another three standing on the other side. The men standing are armed with a variety of weapons - one of them, a huge man, is armed with a lochaber axe - and they look as if they know how to use them.

"...orders from Prince Wladyslaw," the seated soldier is saying to the swordsmen. "The knight they sent has managed to get into the High Castle. The Prince didn't think he would get this far. You are to guard the entrance to the Bell Tower and if the knight manages to evade the rest of the men - kill him."

The swordsmen smile wickedly then turn and walk away. The seated soldier leans back in his chair, puts his feet up onto the desk and starts to clean his fingernails with a dagger.

So, not only has Wladyslaw broken the terms of the challenge by keeping some of his army in the castle, but he has decided to cheat by having you killed as he is obviously too craven to face you alone. Well, you will have to deal with these swordsmen and then teach Wladyslaw that nobody double-crosses Alaric Blackmoon!

Larder next to Kitchen
You are in a larder on the east side of a large kitchen. About 3 or 4 metres away to the West, in the kitchen itself, is a firepit over which a large cauldron of broth is heating up. In the main part of the kitchen to the west you see several mercenaries sitting around a table as well as a cook sitting on a bench near the fire.

You quickly duck back into a corner when you see the mercenaries in the kitchen beyond. They cannot see you but you had better act fast before you are discovered!

> search larder

> throw henbane into cauldron
Using an underarm motion, you lob the henbane through the air towards the bubbling cauldron of broth, where it lands with a PLOP! The mercenary cook starts at the sound and looks around in alarm. Luckily for you he just looks puzzled, gets to his feet and gives the broth a stir with his spoon, then he settles down to snooze once again.

> z

> z

You wait for a while.....and a couple of minutes of time go by without you doing anything.

A few minutes go by and then the cook snorts and, belching loudly, gets to his feet. He takes a sip of the broth with his ladle and nods. Taking a pile of bowls from a nearby shelf, he starts to dish out portions of broth.

"OK, you miserable bunch of cut-throats," he calls out, "grub's up!".

The mercenaries get to their feet as one man with various ribald and extremely rude comments. They each take a dish of broth and sit back down to eat it. The cook joins them, obviously eager to taste his own cooking.

They all seem to be enjoying the broth, but then one of the mercenaries starts to cough and he lurches to his feet holding his throat. The other mercenaries look at him incredulously as he stands there struggling to breathe.

Then - one-by-one - they all follow suit, ending with the cook who is the last to succumb to the poison. Soon, there is silence, punctuated only by the bubbling of the broth above the firepit. The mercenaries all appear to be dead. Now it is safe to venture forth.

Corridor in Undercroft
You are in a corridor in the undercroft of the High Castle. A doorway leads north into a kitchen and the corridor continues South. About 5 metres further along the corridor to the south you see a mercenary lounging on a chair behind a desk.

The mercenary guard seated with his back to you seems unaware of the drama that went on in the kitchen, but you had better deal with him quickly before he becomes alerted to your presence.

> creep up on guard

You creep up behind the guard, raising your sword to slash at him. His soldier's sixth sense gives him warning and he rolls out of the chair, drawing his longsword to parry your attack, responding with some sword thrusts that you are hard put to ward off.

You manage to repel the mercenary's attack with your sword and shield. He is a master swordsman and he tries getting past your defence with his dagger, but you are alert to such tactics.

The sword fight goes on for several minutes with neither of you getting the upper hand, your shield preventing him from getting through your guard on several occasions and your chainmail deflecting a couple of thrusts that did get through.

Eventually, however, your greater stamina begins to tell and you are able to overwhelm his defence and kill him with a sword thrust that pierces his throat and up into his brain!

"...so we need to finish this and be out of here by nightfall," one of the mercenaries says to the other two. "You two go and guard the door to the church where Wladyslaw is and I will go look for the knight."

The first mercenary who was talking walks away into the High Castle, while the other two mercenaries turn and walk off into the High Castle a different way.

Maybe you should follow them to see where they lead you?
